<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Water_management_in_Greater_Mexico_City" title="Water management in Greater Mexico City">Water management in Greater Mexico City</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Xochimilco_trajineras.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Xochimilco_trajineras.jpg/220px-Xochimilco_trajineras.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Xochimilco_trajineras.jpg/330px-Xochimilco_trajineras.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Xochimilco_trajineras.jpg/440px-Xochimilco_trajineras.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Xochimilco_trajineras.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trajinera" title="Trajinera">Trajineras</a> in the canals of <a href="/wiki/Xochimilco" title="Xochimilco">Xochimilco</a>. Xochimilco and the historic center of Mexico City were declared a <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> in 1987.</div></div></div>
<p>Originally much of the valley lay beneath the waters of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Texcoco" title="Lake Texcoco">Lake Texcoco</a>, a system of interconnected salt and freshwater lakes. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aztec" title="Aztec">Aztecs</a> built dikes to separate the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freshwater" title="Freshwater">fresh water</a> used to raise crops in <i><a href="/wiki/Chinampa" title="Chinampa">chinampas</a></i> and to prevent recurrent floods. These dikes were destroyed during the siege of Tenochtitlan, and during colonial times the Spanish regularly drained the lake to prevent floods. Only a small section of the original lake remains, located outside Mexico City, in the municipality of <a href="/wiki/San_Salvador_Atenco" title="San Salvador Atenco">Atenco</a>, <a href="/wiki/State_of_Mexico" title="State of Mexico">State of Mexico</a>.
</p><p>Architects <a href="/wiki/Teodoro_Gonz%C3%A1lez_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Teodoro González de León">Teodoro González de León</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Kalach" title="Alberto Kalach">Alberto Kalach</a> along with a group of Mexican urbanists, engineers and biologists have developed the project plan for <i>Recovering the City of Lakes</i>. If approved by the government the project will contribute to the supply of water from natural sources to the <a href="/wiki/Valley_of_Mexico" title="Valley of Mexico">Valley of Mexico</a>, the creation of new natural spaces, a great improvement in air quality, and greater population establishment planning.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Pollution">Pollution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Pollution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution_in_Mexico_City" title="Air pollution in Mexico City">Air pollution in Mexico City</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AerialViewPhotochemicalSmogMexicoCity_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1936" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/AerialViewPhotochemicalSmogMexicoCity_2.jpg/220px-AerialViewPhotochemicalSmogMexicoCity_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/AerialViewPhotochemicalSmogMexicoCity_2.jpg/330px-AerialViewPhotochemicalSmogMexicoCity_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/AerialViewPhotochemicalSmogMexicoCity_2.jpg/440px-AerialViewPhotochemicalSmogMexicoCity_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AerialViewPhotochemicalSmogMexicoCity_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Air pollution over Mexico City. Air quality is poorest during the winter.</div></div></div>
<p>By the 1990s Mexico City had become infamous as one of the world's most polluted cities; however, the city has since become a model for drastically lowering pollution levels. By 2014 <a href="/wiki/Carbon_monoxide" title="Carbon monoxide">carbon monoxide</a> pollution had dropped drastically, while <a href="/wiki/Sulfur_dioxide" title="Sulfur dioxide">sulfur dioxide</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_dioxide" title="Nitrogen dioxide">nitrogen dioxide</a> were at levels about a third of those in 1992. The levels of signature pollutants in Mexico City are similar to those of <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[78]</a></sup> Despite the cleanup, the metropolitan area is still the most <a href="/wiki/Ozone" title="Ozone">ozone</a>-polluted part of the country, with ozone levels 2.5 times beyond <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/WHO" title="WHO">WHO</a>-defined safe limits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-harvard_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-harvard-80">[79]</a></sup>
</p><p>To clean up pollution, the federal and local governments implemented numerous plans including the constant monitoring and reporting of environmental conditions, such as ozone and <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_oxide" title="Nitrogen oxide">nitrogen oxides</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clean_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-clean-81">[80]</a></sup> When the levels of these two pollutants reached critical levels, contingency actions were implemented which included closing factories, changing school hours, and extending the <i><a href="/wiki/Hoy_No_Circula" title="Hoy No Circula">A day without a car</a></i> program to two days of the week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clean_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-clean-81">[80]</a></sup> The government also instituted industrial technology improvements, a strict biannual vehicle emission inspection and the reformulation of gasoline and <a href="/wiki/Diesel_fuel" title="Diesel fuel">diesel fuels</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-clean_81-2"><a href="#cite_note-clean-81">[80]</a></sup> The introduction of <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_Metrob%C3%BAs" title="Mexico City Metrobús">Metrobús</a> <a href="/wiki/Bus_rapid_transit" title="Bus rapid transit">bus rapid transit</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EcoBici_(Mexico_City)" title="EcoBici (Mexico City)">Ecobici</a> bike-sharing were among efforts to encourage alternate, greener forms of transportation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-harvard_80-1"><a href="#cite_note-harvard-80">[79]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_recreation">Parks and recreation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Parks and recreation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sobrevuelos_CDMX_HJ2A5116_(26515134738).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1667" data-file-width="2500" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Sobrevuelos_CDMX_HJ2A5116_%2826515134738%29.jpg/220px-Sobrevuelos_CDMX_HJ2A5116_%2826515134738%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Sobrevuelos_CDMX_HJ2A5116_%2826515134738%29.jpg/330px-Sobrevuelos_CDMX_HJ2A5116_%2826515134738%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e7/Sobrevuelos_CDMX_HJ2A5116_%2826515134738%29.jpg/440px-Sobrevuelos_CDMX_HJ2A5116_%2826515134738%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sobrevuelos_CDMX_HJ2A5116_(26515134738).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Chapultepec" title="Chapultepec">Chapultepec</a> was an important park during the Aztecs whose access had been limited to its <a href="/wiki/Pipiltin" title="Pipiltin">nobility</a>, was declared open to the public by a decree of <a href="/wiki/Charles_V,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor">Charles V, Holy Roman Emperor</a> in 1530,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NY_Times_1987-12-13_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Times_1987-12-13-82">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> it is one of the world's largest city parks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NY_Times_1987-12-13_82-1"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Times_1987-12-13-82">[81]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Chapultepec" title="Chapultepec">Chapultepec</a>, the city's most iconic public park, has history back to the Aztec emperors who used the area as a retreat. It is south of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polanco_(Mexico)" title="Polanco (Mexico)">Polanco</a> district, and houses the <a href="/wiki/Chapultepec_Zoo" title="Chapultepec Zoo">Chapultepec Zoo</a> the main city's zoo, several ponds and seven museums, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Museo_Nacional_de_Antropolog%C3%ADa" title="Museo Nacional de Antropología">National Museum of Anthropology</a>. Other iconic city parks include the <a href="/wiki/Alameda_Central" title="Alameda Central">Alameda Central</a>, it is recognized as the oldest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_park" title="Public park">public park</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Parque_M%C3%A9xico" title="Parque México">Parque México</a> and <a href="/wiki/Parque_Espa%C3%B1a" title="Parque España">Parque España</a> in the hip <a href="/wiki/Condesa" title="Condesa">Condesa</a> district; <a href="/wiki/Parque_Hundido" title="Parque Hundido">Parque Hundido</a> and <i>Parque de los Venados</i> in <a href="/wiki/Colonia_del_Valle" title="Colonia del Valle">Colonia del Valle</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Parque_Lincoln" title="Parque Lincoln">Parque Lincoln</a> in <a href="/wiki/Polanco,_Mexico_City" title="Polanco, Mexico City">Polanco</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup> There are many smaller parks throughout the city. Most are small "squares" occupying two or three square blocks amid residential or commercial districts. Several other larger parks such as the Bosque de Tlalpan and <a href="/wiki/Viveros_de_Coyoac%C3%A1n" title="Viveros de Coyoacán">Viveros de Coyoacán</a>, and in the east <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Alameda_Oriente&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Alameda Oriente (page does not exist)">Alameda Oriente</a>, offer many recreational activities. Northwest of the city is a large ecological reserve, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bosque_de_Arag%C3%B3n&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bosque de Aragón (page does not exist)">Bosque de Aragón</a>. In the southeast is the <a href="/wiki/Xochimilco_Ecological_Park_and_Plant_Market" title="Xochimilco Ecological Park and Plant Market">Xochimilco Ecological Park and Plant Market</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Heritage_site" title="World Heritage site">World Heritage site</a>. West of <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe,_Mexico_City" title="Santa Fe, Mexico City">Santa Fe</a> district are the pine forests of the <a href="/wiki/Desierto_de_los_Leones_National_Park" title="Desierto de los Leones National Park">Desierto de los Leones National Park</a>. Amusement parks include <a href="/wiki/Six_Flags_M%C3%A9xico" title="Six Flags México">Six Flags México</a>, in Ajusco neighborhood which is the largest in Latin America. There are numerous seasonal fairs present in the city.
</p><p>Mexico City has three zoos. <a href="/wiki/Chapultepec_Zoo" title="Chapultepec Zoo">Chapultepec Zoo</a>, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=San_Juan_de_Aragon_Zoo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="San Juan de Aragon Zoo (page does not exist)">San Juan de Aragon Zoo</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Los_Coyotes_Zoo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Los Coyotes Zoo (page does not exist)">Los Coyotes Zoo</a>. Chapultepec Zoo is located in the first section of Chapultepec Park in the Miguel Hidalgo. It was opened in 1924.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup> Visitors can see about 243 specimens of different species including kangaroos, giant panda, gorillas, caracal, hyena, hippos, jaguar, giraffe, lemur, lion, among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup> Zoo San Juan de Aragon is near the San Juan de Aragon Park in the Gustavo A. Madero. In this zoo, opened in 1964,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup> there are species that are in danger of extinction such as the jaguar and the Mexican wolf. Other guests are the golden eagle, pronghorn, bighorn sheep, caracara, zebras, African elephant, macaw, hippo, among others.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[89]</a></sup> Zoo Los Coyotes is a 27.68-acre (11.2 ha) zoo located south of Mexico City in the Coyoacan. It was inaugurated on 2 February 1999.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> It has more than 301 specimens of 51 species of wild native or endemic fauna from the area, featuring eagles, ajolotes, coyotes, macaws, bobcats, Mexican wolves, raccoons, mountain lions, teporingos, foxes, white-tailed deer.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:B_(70011807).jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1512" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/B_%2870011807%29.jpeg/220px-B_%2870011807%29.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/B_%2870011807%29.jpeg/330px-B_%2870011807%29.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/B_%2870011807%29.jpeg/440px-B_%2870011807%29.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:B_(70011807).jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">Lightning</a> in the background of the <a href="/wiki/Torre_Mayor" title="Torre Mayor">Torre Mayor</a></div></div></div>
<p>Mexico City has a <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">subtropical highland climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> <i>Cwb</i>), due to its tropical location but high elevation. The lower region of the valley receives less rainfall than the upper regions of the south; the lower boroughs of <a href="/wiki/Iztapalapa" title="Iztapalapa">Iztapalapa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Iztacalco" title="Iztacalco">Iztacalco</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venustiano_Carranza,_D.F." title="Venustiano Carranza, D.F.">Venustiano Carranza</a> and the east portion of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gustavo_A._Madero,_D.F." title="Gustavo A. Madero, D.F.">Gustavo A. Madero</a> are usually drier and warmer than the upper southern boroughs of <a href="/wiki/Tlalpan" title="Tlalpan">Tlalpan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Milpa_Alta" title="Milpa Alta">Milpa Alta</a>, a mountainous region of <a href="/wiki/Pine" title="Pine">pine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">oak</a> trees known as the range of <a href="/wiki/Ajusco" title="Ajusco">Ajusco</a>. The average annual temperature varies from 12 to 16 °C (54 to 61 °F), depending on the altitude of the borough. The temperature is rarely below 3 °C (37 °F) or above 30 °C (86 °F).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weatherspark_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-weatherspark-93">[92]</a></sup> At the Tacubaya observatory, the lowest temperature ever registered was −4.4 °C (24 °F) on 13 February 1960, and the highest temperature on record was 33.9 °C (93 °F) on 9 May 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Extreme_temps_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-Extreme_temps-94">[93]</a></sup> Overall precipitation is heavily concentrated in the summer months, and includes dense <a href="/wiki/Hail" title="Hail">hail</a>.
</p><p>Snow falls in the city very rarely, although somewhat more often in nearby mountain tops. Throughout its history, the Central Valley of Mexico was accustomed to having several snowfalls per decade (including a period between 1878 and 1895 in which every single year—except 1880—recorded snowfalls<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clima-CDMX_95-0"><a href="#cite_note-Clima-CDMX-95">[94]</a></sup>) mostly <a href="/wiki/Lake-effect_snow" title="Lake-effect snow">lake-effect snow</a>. The effects of the draining of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Texcoco" title="Lake Texcoco">Lake Texcoco</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> have greatly reduced snowfalls after the snow flurries of 12 February 1907.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> Since 1908, snow has only fallen three times, snow on 14 February 1920;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> snow flurries on 14 March 1940;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> and on 12 January 1967, when 8 centimeters (3 in) of snow fell on the city, the most on record.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> The 1967 snowstorm coincided with the operation of <i><a href="/wiki/Lake_Texcoco#Artificial_drainage" title="Lake Texcoco">Deep Drainage System</a></i> that resulted in the total draining of what was left of Lake Texcoco.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clima-CDMX_95-1"><a href="#cite_note-Clima-CDMX-95">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DAMsxix_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-DAMsxix-100">[99]</a></sup> After the disappearance of Lake Texcoco, snow has never fallen again over Mexico City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Clima-CDMX_95-2"><a href="#cite_note-Clima-CDMX-95">[94]</a></sup> The region of the <a href="/wiki/Valley_of_Mexico" title="Valley of Mexico">Valley of Mexico</a> receives <a href="/wiki/Anticyclone" title="Anticyclone">anti-cyclonic</a> systems. The weak winds of these systems do not allow for the dispersion, outside the basin, of the <a href="/wiki/Air_pollution" title="Air pollution">air pollutants</a> which are produced by the 50,000 industries and 4 million vehicles operating in and around the metropolitan area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup>
</p><p>The area receives about 820 millimeters (32 in) of annual rainfall, which is concentrated from May through October with little or no precipitation the remainder of the year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-National_Research_75-3"><a href="#cite_note-National_Research-75">[74]</a></sup> The area has two main seasons. The wet humid summer runs from May to October when winds bring in tropical moisture from the sea, the wettest month being July. The cool sunny winter runs from November to April, when the air is relatively drier, the driest month being December. This season is subdivided into a cold winter period and a warm spring period. The cold period spans from November to February, when polar <a href="/wiki/Air_mass" title="Air mass">air masses</a> push down from the north and keep the air fairly dry. The warm period extends from March to May when subtropical winds again dominate but do not yet carry enough moisture for rain to form.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lafragua_2003_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lafragua_2003-102">[101]</a></sup>
</p>
