<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="toccolours" style="width:15em;border-top-width:0;border-spacing: 0;float:right;clear:right;margin:0.5em 0 1em 0.5em;"><caption style="border-top:1px #aaa solid;border-left:1px #aaa solid;border-right:1px #aaa solid;background-color:lavender;padding:0.25em;font-weight:bold">Historical population</caption><tbody><tr style="font-size:95%"><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;width:3em">Year</th><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px 2px;text-align:right"><abbr title="Population">Pop.</abbr></th><th style="border-bottom:1px solid black;padding:1px;text-align:right"><abbr title="Percent change">±%</abbr></th></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1950</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">3,365,081</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">—    </td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1960</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">5,479,184</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+62.8%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1970</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">8,830,947</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+61.2%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">1980</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">13,027,620</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+47.5%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">1990</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">15,642,318</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px;border-bottom:1px solid #bbbbbb">+20.1%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2000</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">18,457,027</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+18.0%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2010</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">20,136,681</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+9.1%</td></tr><tr><th style="text-align:center;padding:1px">2019</th><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">21,671,908</td><td style="text-align:right;padding:1px">+7.6%</td></tr><tr><td colspan="3" style="border-top:1px solid black;font-size:85%;text-align:left">for Mexico City Agglomeration:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Historically, and since <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era" title="Pre-Columbian era">Pre-Columbian</a> times, the <a href="/wiki/Valley_of_Mexico" title="Valley of Mexico">Valley of Anahuac</a> has been one of the most densely populated areas in Mexico. When the Federal District was created in 1824, the urban area of Mexico City extended approximately to the area of today's <a href="/wiki/Cuauht%C3%A9moc,_Mexico_City" title="Cuauhtémoc, Mexico City">Cuauhtémoc borough</a>. At the beginning of the 20th century, the <i>elites</i> began migrating to the south and west and soon the small towns of <a href="/wiki/Mixcoac" title="Mixcoac">Mixcoac</a> and <a href="/wiki/San_%C3%81ngel" title="San Ángel">San Ángel</a> were incorporated by the growing conurbation. According to the 1921 census, 54.78% of the city's population was considered Mestizo (Indigenous mixed with European), 22.79% considered European, and 18.74% considered Indigenous.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> This was the last Mexican Census which asked people to self-identify with a heritage other than Amerindian. In 1921, Mexico City had less than one million inhabitants.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2022)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Up to the 1990s, the Federal District was the most populous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_divisions_of_Mexico" title="Political divisions of Mexico">federal entity</a> in Mexico, but since then, its population has remained stable at around 8.7 million. The growth of the city has extended beyond the limits of the city to 59 municipalities of the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Mexico" title="State of Mexico">State of Mexico</a> and 1 in the state of <a href="/wiki/Hidalgo_(state)" title="Hidalgo (state)">Hidalgo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CONAPOzm2005_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-CONAPOzm2005-108">[107]</a></sup> With a population of approximately 19.8 million inhabitants (2008),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CONAPOProy2_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-CONAPOProy2-109">[108]</a></sup> it is one of the most populous conurbations in the world. Nonetheless, the annual rate of growth of the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Mexico_City" title="Greater Mexico City">Metropolitan Area of Mexico City</a> is much lower than that of other large urban agglomerations in Mexico,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sintesis_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sintesis-110">[109]</a></sup> a phenomenon most likely attributable to the <a href="/wiki/Environmental_policy" title="Environmental policy">environmental policy</a> of decentralization. The <a href="/wiki/Net_migration_rate" title="Net migration rate">net migration rate</a> of Mexico City from 1995 to 2000 was negative.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metropolitan_area">Metropolitan area</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Metropolitan area">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Greater_Mexico_City" title="Greater Mexico City">Greater Mexico City</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mexico_City_Metropolitan_Area_Map.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="765" data-file-width="667" decoding="async" height="252" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Mexico_City_Metropolitan_Area_Map.svg/220px-Mexico_City_Metropolitan_Area_Map.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Mexico_City_Metropolitan_Area_Map.svg/330px-Mexico_City_Metropolitan_Area_Map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Mexico_City_Metropolitan_Area_Map.svg/440px-Mexico_City_Metropolitan_Area_Map.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mexico_City_Metropolitan_Area_Map.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Greater_Mexico_City" title="Greater Mexico City">Greater Mexico City</a> and Mexico City</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Greater_Mexico_City" title="Greater Mexico City">Greater Mexico City</a> is formed by Mexico City, 60 municipalities from the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Mexico" title="State of Mexico">State of Mexico</a> and one from the state of <a href="/wiki/Hidalgo_(state)" title="Hidalgo (state)">Hidalgo</a>. Greater Mexico City is the <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_areas_of_Mexico" title="Metropolitan areas of Mexico">largest metropolitan area in Mexico</a> and the area with the highest population density. As of 2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, 21,804,515 people live in this urban agglomeration, of which 9,209,944 live in Mexico City proper.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inegi_pop_2020_9-2"><a href="#cite_note-inegi_pop_2020-9">[9]</a></sup> In terms of population, the biggest municipalities that are part of Greater Mexico City (excluding Mexico City proper) are in the State of Mexico:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inegi_pop_2020_9-3"><a href="#cite_note-inegi_pop_2020-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ecatepec_de_Morelos" title="Ecatepec de Morelos">Ecatepec de Morelos</a> (<abbr title="population">pop.</abbr> 1,645,352)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ciudad_Nezahualc%C3%B3yotl" title="Ciudad Nezahualcóyotl">Nezahualcóyotl</a> (<abbr title="population">pop.</abbr> 1,077,208)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Naucalpan" title="Naucalpan">Naucalpan</a> (<abbr title="population">pop.</abbr> 834,434)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Chimalhuac%C3%A1n" title="Chimalhuacán">Chimalhuacán</a> (<abbr title="population">pop.</abbr> 705,193)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tlalnepantla_de_Baz" title="Tlalnepantla de Baz">Tlalnepantla de Baz</a> (<abbr title="population">pop.</abbr> 672,202)</li></ul>
<p>Approximately 75% (10 million) of the State of México's population live in municipalities that are part of Greater Mexico City. Greater Mexico City was the fastest growing metropolitan area in the country until the late 1980s. Since then, and through a policy of decentralization in order to reduce the environmental pollutants of the growing conurbation, the annual rate of growth of the agglomeration has decreased, and it is lower than that of the other four largest metropolitan areas (namely <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Guadalajara" title="Greater Guadalajara">Greater Guadalajara</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Monterrey" title="Greater Monterrey">Greater Monterrey</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greater_Puebla" title="Greater Puebla">Greater Puebla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Greater_Toluca" title="Greater Toluca">Greater Toluca</a>) even though it is still positive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sintesis_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-Sintesis-110">[109]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Net_migration_rate" title="Net migration rate">net migration rate</a> of Mexico City proper from 1995 to 2000 was negative,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup> which implies that residents are moving to the suburbs of the metropolitan area, or to other states of Mexico. In addition, some inner suburbs are losing population to outer suburbs, indicating the continuing expansion of Greater Mexico City.
</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:2208px"><div class="thumbinner"><div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Panorama_of_Mexico_City_from_Torre_Latinoamericana.jpg" title="Panorama of Mexico City from Torre Latinoamericana"><img alt="" data-file-height="2306" data-file-width="24115" decoding="async" height="210" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Panorama_of_Mexico_City_from_Torre_Latinoamericana.jpg/2200px-Panorama_of_Mexico_City_from_Torre_Latinoamericana.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Panorama_of_Mexico_City_from_Torre_Latinoamericana.jpg/3300px-Panorama_of_Mexico_City_from_Torre_Latinoamericana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Panorama_of_Mexico_City_from_Torre_Latinoamericana.jpg/4400px-Panorama_of_Mexico_City_from_Torre_Latinoamericana.jpg 2x" width="2200"/></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Panorama_of_Mexico_City_from_Torre_Latinoamericana.jpg" title="File:Panorama of Mexico City from Torre Latinoamericana.jpg"> </a></div>Panorama of Mexico City from <a href="/wiki/Torre_Latinoamericana" title="Torre Latinoamericana">Torre Latinoamericana</a></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:D%C3%ADa_de_la_virgen.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2620" data-file-width="3932" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/D%C3%ADa_de_la_virgen.jpg/220px-D%C3%ADa_de_la_virgen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/D%C3%ADa_de_la_virgen.jpg/330px-D%C3%ADa_de_la_virgen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/D%C3%ADa_de_la_virgen.jpg/440px-D%C3%ADa_de_la_virgen.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:D%C3%ADa_de_la_virgen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Our_Lady_of_Guadalupe" title="Basilica of Our Lady of Guadalupe">Basilica of Our Lady of Guadalupe</a> in <a href="/wiki/Villa_de_Guadalupe,_Mexico_City" title="Villa de Guadalupe, Mexico City">La Villa de Guadalupe</a>, the main <a href="/wiki/Christian_pilgrimage" title="Christian pilgrimage">Catholic pilgrimage</a> site in the Americas. It houses the original image of <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Guadalupe" title="Our Lady of Guadalupe">Our Lady of Guadalupe</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>The majority (82%) of the residents in Mexico City are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic" title="Catholic">Catholic</a>, slightly lower than the 2010 census national percentage of 87%, making it the largest <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> denomination, though it has been decreasing over the last decades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> Many other religions and philosophies are also practiced in the city: many different types of <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> groups, different types of <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Mexico" title="History of the Jews in Mexico">Jewish communities</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">Buddhist</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Islamic" title="Islamic">Islamic</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Spirituality" title="Spirituality">spiritual</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philosophical" title="Philosophical">philosophical</a> groups. There are also growing<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup> numbers of irreligious people, whether <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agnostic" title="Agnostic">agnostic</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atheist" title="Atheist">atheist</a>.
The patron saint of Mexico City is Saint <a href="/wiki/Philip_of_Jesus" title="Philip of Jesus">Philip of Jesus</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_people" title="Mexican people">Mexican</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic" title="Catholic">Catholic</a> missionary who became one of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Twenty-six_Martyrs_of_Japan" title="Twenty-six Martyrs of Japan">Twenty-six Martyrs of Japan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Mexico" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Mexico">Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Mexico</a> is the largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archdiocese" title="Archdiocese">archdiocese</a> in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> There are two Catholic cathedrals in the city, the <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_Metropolitan_Cathedral" title="Mexico City Metropolitan Cathedral">Mexico City Metropolitan Cathedral</a> and the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Iztapalapa_Cathedral,_Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Iztapalapa Cathedral, Mexico City (page does not exist)">Iztapalapa Cathedral</a>, and three former Catholic churches who are now the cathedrals of other rites, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=San_Jos%C3%A9_de_Gracia_Cathedral,_Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="San José de Gracia Cathedral, Mexico City (page does not exist)">San José de Gracia Cathedral</a> (Anglican church), the <a href="/wiki/Porta_Coeli_Cathedral,_Mexico_City" title="Porta Coeli Cathedral, Mexico City">Porta Coeli Cathedral</a> (Melkite Greek Catholic church) and the <a href="/wiki/Valvanera_Cathedral,_Mexico_City" title="Valvanera Cathedral, Mexico City">Valvanera Cathedral</a> (Maronite church).
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Mexico City is also home to large communities of <a href="/wiki/Expatriate" title="Expatriate">expatriates</a> and immigrants from the rest of North America (U.S. and Canada), from South America (mainly from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Argentine_people" title="Argentine people">Argentina</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colombian_people" title="Colombian people">Colombia</a>, but also from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brazilian_people" title="Brazilian people">Brazil</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chilean_people" title="Chilean people">Chile</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Uruguayan_people" title="Uruguayan people">Uruguay</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venezuelan_people" title="Venezuelan people">Venezuela</a>), from Central America and the Caribbean (mainly from <a href="/wiki/Cubans" title="Cubans">Cuba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Guatemala" title="Demographics of Guatemala">Guatemala</a>, <a href="/wiki/List_of_Salvadorans" title="List of Salvadorans">El Salvador</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Haitian_people" title="Haitian people">Haiti</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hondurans" title="Hondurans">Honduras</a>); from Europe (mainly from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spanish_people" title="Spanish people">Spain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swiss_people" title="Swiss people">Switzerland</a>, but also from <a href="/wiki/Czechs" title="Czechs">Czech Republic</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hungarian_people" title="Hungarian people">Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">France</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_people" title="Italian people">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Irish_people" title="Irish people">Ireland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">the Netherlands</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polish_people" title="Polish people">Poland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romanians" title="Romanians">Romania</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-extranjeros_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-extranjeros-117">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> and from the Arab world (mostly from Lebanon, and other countries like Syria and Egypt).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[118]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mexico City is home to the largest population of <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_United_States" title="Demographics of the United States">Americans</a> living outside the United States. Estimates are as high as 700,000 Americans living in Mexico City, while in 1999 the U.S. Bureau of Consular Affairs estimated over 440,000 Americans lived in the Mexico City Metropolitan Area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup>
</p><p>Representing around 18.74% of the city's population, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_in_Mexico" title="Indigenous peoples in Mexico">indigenous peoples</a> from different areas of Mexico have migrated to the capital in search of better economic opportunities. <a href="/wiki/Nahuatl" title="Nahuatl">Nahuatl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Otomi_language" title="Otomi language">Otomi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mixtec" title="Mixtec">Mixtec</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zapotec_languages" title="Zapotec languages">Zapotec</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mazahua_language" title="Mazahua language">Mazahua</a> are the indigenous languages with the greatest number of speakers in Mexico City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> According to the 2020 Census, 2.03% of Mexico City's population identified as Black, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afro-Mexican" title="Afro-Mexican">Afro-Mexican</a>, or of African descent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Centro_M%C3%A9dico_Nacional_Siglo_XXI_-_2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="5472" data-file-width="7296" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Centro_M%C3%A9dico_Nacional_Siglo_XXI_-_2.jpg/220px-Centro_M%C3%A9dico_Nacional_Siglo_XXI_-_2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Centro_M%C3%A9dico_Nacional_Siglo_XXI_-_2.jpg/330px-Centro_M%C3%A9dico_Nacional_Siglo_XXI_-_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Centro_M%C3%A9dico_Nacional_Siglo_XXI_-_2.jpg/440px-Centro_M%C3%A9dico_Nacional_Siglo_XXI_-_2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Centro_M%C3%A9dico_Nacional_Siglo_XXI_-_2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/XXI_Century_National_Medical_Center" title="XXI Century National Medical Center">XXI Century National Medical Center</a>, managed by the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Social_Security_Institute" title="Mexican Social Security Institute">Mexican Social Security Institute</a> (IMSS)</div></div></div>
<p>Mexico City is home to some of the best private hospitals in the country, including Hospital Ángeles, Hospital ABC and Médica Sur. The national <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Publicly-funded_health_care" title="Publicly-funded health care">public healthcare</a> institution for <a href="/wiki/Private_sector" title="Private sector">private-sector</a> employees, <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Social_Security_Institute" title="Mexican Social Security Institute">IMSS</a>, has its largest facilities in Mexico City—including the National Medical Center and the <a href="/wiki/La_Raza" title="La Raza">La Raza</a> Medical Center—and has an annual budget of over 6 billion pesos. The IMSS and other <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">public health</a> institutions, including the ISSSTE (Public Sector Employees' Social Security Institute) and the National Health Ministry (SSA) maintain large specialty facilities in the city. These include the National Institutes of Cardiology, Nutrition, Psychiatry, Oncology, Pediatrics, Rehabilitation, among others.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Group" title="World Bank Group">World Bank</a> has sponsored a project to curb air pollution through public transport improvements and the Mexican government has started shutting down polluting factories. They have phased out diesel buses and mandated new emission controls on new cars; since 1993 all new cars must be fitted with a <a href="/wiki/Catalytic_converter" title="Catalytic converter">catalytic converter</a>, which reduces the emissions released. Trucks must use only <a href="/wiki/Liquefied_petroleum_gas" title="Liquefied petroleum gas">liquefied petroleum gas</a> (LPG). Also construction of an <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_Metro" title="Mexico City Metro">underground rail system</a> was begun in 1968 in order to help curb air pollution problems and alleviate <a href="/wiki/Traffic_congestion" title="Traffic congestion">traffic congestion</a>. It has over 201 km (125 mi) of track and carries over 5 million people every day. Fees are kept low to encourage use of the system and during <a href="/wiki/Rush_hour" title="Rush hour">rush hours</a> the crush is so great, that authorities have reserved a special carriage specifically for women. Due to these initiatives and others, the air quality in Mexico City has begun to improve; it is cleaner than it was in 1991, when the air quality was declared to be a public health risk for 355 days of the year.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2012)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Explanada_de_El_Colegio_de_M%C3%A9xico.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="600" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Explanada_de_El_Colegio_de_M%C3%A9xico.jpg/220px-Explanada_de_El_Colegio_de_M%C3%A9xico.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Explanada_de_El_Colegio_de_M%C3%A9xico.jpg/330px-Explanada_de_El_Colegio_de_M%C3%A9xico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Explanada_de_El_Colegio_de_M%C3%A9xico.jpg/440px-Explanada_de_El_Colegio_de_M%C3%A9xico.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Explanada_de_El_Colegio_de_M%C3%A9xico.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/El_Colegio_de_M%C3%A9xico" title="El Colegio de México">El Colegio de México</a></div></div></div>
<p>Unlike those of Mexican states' schools, curricula of Mexico City's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_school_(government_funded)" title="Public school (government funded)">public schools</a> is managed by the federal <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secretariat_of_Public_Education" title="Secretariat of Public Education">Secretary of Public Education</a>. The whole funding is allocated by the government of Mexico City (in some specific cases, such as <a href="/wiki/El_Colegio_de_M%C3%A9xico" title="El Colegio de México">El Colegio de México</a>, funding comes from both the city's government and other public and private national and international entities).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The city's public high school system is the <i><a href="/wiki/Instituto_de_Educaci%C3%B3n_Media_Superior_de_la_Ciudad_de_M%C3%A9xico" title="Instituto de Educación Media Superior de la Ciudad de México">Instituto de Educación Media Superior de la Ciudad de México</a></i> (IEMS-DF). A special case is that of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colegio_Nacional_(Mexico)" title="Colegio Nacional (Mexico)">El Colegio Nacional</a>, created during the district's governmental period of <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Alem%C3%A1n_Vald%C3%A9s" title="Miguel Alemán Valdés">Miguel Alemán Valdés</a> to have, in Mexico, an institution similar to the <a href="/wiki/Coll%C3%A8ge_de_France" title="Collège de France">College of France</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Among its many public and private schools (K–13), the city offers <a href="/wiki/Multiculturalism" title="Multiculturalism">multi-cultural</a>, <a href="/wiki/Multilingualism" title="Multilingualism">multi-lingual</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_school" title="International school">international schools</a> attended by Mexican and <a href="/wiki/International_student" title="International student">foreign students</a>. Best known are the <a href="/wiki/Colegio_Alem%C3%A1n_Alexander_von_Humboldt_(Mexico_City)" title="Colegio Alemán Alexander von Humboldt (Mexico City)">Colegio Alemán</a> (German school with three main campuses), the <a href="/wiki/Liceo_Mexicano_Japon%C3%A9s" title="Liceo Mexicano Japonés">Liceo Mexicano Japonés</a> (Japanese), the Centro Cultural Coreano en México (Korean), the <a href="/wiki/Lyc%C3%A9e_Franco-Mexicain" title="Lycée Franco-Mexicain">Lycée Franco-Mexicain</a> (French), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ASF_Mexico" title="ASF Mexico">American School</a>, The <a href="/wiki/Westhill_Institute" title="Westhill Institute">Westhill Institute</a> (American School), the <a href="/wiki/Edron_Academy" title="Edron Academy">Edron Academy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Greengates_School" title="Greengates School">Greengates School</a> (British). Mexico City joined the UNESCO Global Network of Learning Cities in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Plaza_de_las_Tres_Culturas" title="Plaza de las Tres Culturas">Plaza de las Tres Culturas</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Colegio_de_Santa_Cruz_de_Tlatelolco" title="Colegio de Santa Cruz de Tlatelolco">Colegio de Santa Cruz de Tlatelolco</a> that is recognized for being the first and oldest European school of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Higher_learning" title="Higher learning">higher learning</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-catalog.hathitrust.org_125-0"><a href="#cite_note-catalog.hathitrust.org-125">[124]</a></sup> and the first major school of interpreters and translators in the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup> Other, the now-defunct <a href="/wiki/Royal_and_Pontifical_University_of_Mexico" title="Royal and Pontifical University of Mexico">Royal and Pontifical University of Mexico</a> is considered the father of the UNAM, and it was located in the city and was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_colonial_universities_in_Hispanic_America" title="List of colonial universities in Hispanic America">third oldest university in the Americas</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ciudad_Universitaria_(5535011417).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Ciudad_Universitaria_%285535011417%29.jpg/220px-Ciudad_Universitaria_%285535011417%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Ciudad_Universitaria_%285535011417%29.jpg/330px-Ciudad_Universitaria_%285535011417%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Ciudad_Universitaria_%285535011417%29.jpg/440px-Ciudad_Universitaria_%285535011417%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ciudad_Universitaria_(5535011417).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Central Campus of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_City_of_Mexico" title="University City of Mexico">University City</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Autonomous_University_of_Mexico" title="National Autonomous University of Mexico">UNAM</a>. Since 2007 the University City is a UNESCO World Heritage Site.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MexDes_127-0"><a href="#cite_note-MexDes-127">[126]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Autonomous_University_of_Mexico" title="National Autonomous University of Mexico">National Autonomous University of Mexico</a> (UNAM), located in Mexico City, is the largest university on the continent, with more than 300,000 students from all backgrounds. Three <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates" title="List of Nobel laureates">Nobel laureates</a>, several Mexican entrepreneurs and most of Mexico's modern-day presidents are among its former students. UNAM conducts 50% of Mexico's <a href="/wiki/Scientific_method" title="Scientific method">scientific research</a> and has presence all across the country with satellite campuses, observatories and research centers. UNAM ranked 74th in the Top 200 World <a href="/wiki/College_and_university_rankings" title="College and university rankings">University Ranking</a> published by <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education" title="Times Higher Education">Times Higher Education</a> (then called Times Higher Education Supplement) in 2006,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup> making it the highest ranked Spanish-speaking university in the world. The sprawling main campus of the university, known as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_City_of_Mexico" title="University City of Mexico">Ciudad Universitaria</a>, was named a World Heritage Site by UNESCO in 2007.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MexDes_127-1"><a href="#cite_note-MexDes-127">[126]</a></sup>
</p><p>The second largest higher-education institution is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Polytechnic_Institute" title="National Polytechnic Institute">National Polytechnic Institute</a> (IPN), which includes among many other relevant centers the <a href="/wiki/CINVESTAV" title="CINVESTAV">Centro de Investigación y de Estudios Avanzados</a> (Cinvestav), where varied high-level scientific and technological research is done. Other major higher-education institutions in the city include the <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Aut%C3%B3noma_Metropolitana" title="Universidad Autónoma Metropolitana">Metropolitan Autonomous University</a> (UAM), the <a href="/wiki/National_School_of_Anthropology_and_History" title="National School of Anthropology and History">National School of Anthropology and History</a> (ENAH), the <a href="/wiki/Instituto_Tecnol%C3%B3gico_Aut%C3%B3nomo_de_M%C3%A9xico" title="Instituto Tecnológico Autónomo de México">Instituto Tecnológico Autónomo de México</a> (ITAM), the <a href="/wiki/Monterrey_Institute_of_Technology_and_Higher_Education" title="Monterrey Institute of Technology and Higher Education">Monterrey Institute of Technology and Higher Education</a> (3 campuses), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universidad_Panamericana_Sede_M%C3%A9xico" title="Universidad Panamericana Sede México">Universidad Panamericana</a> (UP), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Universidad_La_Salle" title="Universidad La Salle">Universidad La Salle</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Intercontinental" title="Universidad Intercontinental">Universidad Intercontinental</a> (UIC), the <a href="/wiki/Universidad_del_Valle_de_M%C3%A9xico" title="Universidad del Valle de México">Universidad del Valle de México</a> (UVM), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anahuac_Universities_Network" title="Anahuac Universities Network">Universidad Anáhuac</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sim%C3%B3n_Bol%C3%ADvar_University_(Mexico)" title="Simón Bolívar University (Mexico)">Simón Bolívar University</a> (USB), the <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Intercontinental" title="Universidad Intercontinental">Universidad Intercontinental</a> (UIC), the <a href="/wiki/Alliant_International_University" title="Alliant International University">Alliant International University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Iberoamericana" title="Universidad Iberoamericana">Universidad Iberoamericana</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Colegio_de_M%C3%A9xico" title="El Colegio de México">El Colegio de México</a> (Colmex), <a href="/wiki/Escuela_Libre_de_Derecho" title="Escuela Libre de Derecho">Escuela Libre de Derecho</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Centro_de_Investigaci%C3%B3n_y_Docencia_Econ%C3%B3micas" title="Centro de Investigación y Docencia Económicas">Centro de Investigación y Docencia Económica</a>, (CIDE).
In addition, the prestigious <a href="/wiki/University_of_California" title="University of California">University of California</a> maintains a campus known as "Casa de California" in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Universidad_Tecnol%C3%B3gica_de_M%C3%A9xico" title="Universidad Tecnológica de México">Universidad Tecnológica de México</a> is also in Mexico City.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_structure">Political structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Political structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Palacio_Nacional_2012-09-29_22-45-57.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3456" data-file-width="4608" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Palacio_Nacional_2012-09-29_22-45-57.jpg/220px-Palacio_Nacional_2012-09-29_22-45-57.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Palacio_Nacional_2012-09-29_22-45-57.jpg/330px-Palacio_Nacional_2012-09-29_22-45-57.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Palacio_Nacional_2012-09-29_22-45-57.jpg/440px-Palacio_Nacional_2012-09-29_22-45-57.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Palacio_Nacional_2012-09-29_22-45-57.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Palace_of_Mexico" title="National Palace of Mexico">National Palace of Mexico</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Senado_de_M%C3%A9xico_01.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3363" data-file-width="5412" decoding="async" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Senado_de_M%C3%A9xico_01.jpg/220px-Senado_de_M%C3%A9xico_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Senado_de_M%C3%A9xico_01.jpg/330px-Senado_de_M%C3%A9xico_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Senado_de_M%C3%A9xico_01.jpg/440px-Senado_de_M%C3%A9xico_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Senado_de_M%C3%A9xico_01.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Senate_of_the_Republic_(Mexico)" title="Senate of the Republic (Mexico)">Senate of the Republic</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LegPalaceDF.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1571" data-file-width="3872" decoding="async" height="89" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/LegPalaceDF.JPG/220px-LegPalaceDF.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/LegPalaceDF.JPG/330px-LegPalaceDF.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/LegPalaceDF.JPG/440px-LegPalaceDF.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LegPalaceDF.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Legislative_Palace_of_San_L%C3%A1zaro" title="Legislative Palace of San Lázaro">Legislative Palace of San Lázaro</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Edificio_Tlatelolco_(S.R.E).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Edificio_Tlatelolco_%28S.R.E%29.JPG/220px-Edificio_Tlatelolco_%28S.R.E%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Edificio_Tlatelolco_%28S.R.E%29.JPG/330px-Edificio_Tlatelolco_%28S.R.E%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Edificio_Tlatelolco_%28S.R.E%29.JPG/440px-Edificio_Tlatelolco_%28S.R.E%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Edificio_Tlatelolco_(S.R.E).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Offices of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secretariat_of_Foreign_Affairs" title="Secretariat of Foreign Affairs">Secretariat of Foreign Affairs</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:C%C3%A1mara_de_Diputados_2012-09-09_03-36-12.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1836" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/C%C3%A1mara_de_Diputados_2012-09-09_03-36-12.jpg/220px-C%C3%A1mara_de_Diputados_2012-09-09_03-36-12.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/C%C3%A1mara_de_Diputados_2012-09-09_03-36-12.jpg/330px-C%C3%A1mara_de_Diputados_2012-09-09_03-36-12.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/41/C%C3%A1mara_de_Diputados_2012-09-09_03-36-12.jpg/440px-C%C3%A1mara_de_Diputados_2012-09-09_03-36-12.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:C%C3%A1mara_de_Diputados_2012-09-09_03-36-12.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mexico City's Legislative Assembly building</div></div></div>
<p>The Acta Constitutiva de la Federación of 31 January 1824, and the Federal Constitution of 4 October 1824,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup> fixed the political and administrative organization of the <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">United Mexican States</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_War_of_Independence" title="Mexican War of Independence">Mexican War of Independence</a>. In addition, Section XXVIII of Article 50 gave the new Congress the right to choose where the federal government would be located. This location would then be appropriated as federal land, with the federal government acting as the local authority. The two main candidates to become the capital were Mexico City and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quer%C3%A9taro,_Quer%C3%A9taro" title="Querétaro, Querétaro">Querétaro</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup>
</p><p>Due in large part to the persuasion of representative <a href="/wiki/Servando_Teresa_de_Mier" title="Servando Teresa de Mier">Servando Teresa de Mier</a>, Mexico City was chosen because it was the center of the country's population and history, even though Querétaro was closer to the center geographically. The choice was official on 18 November 1824, and Congress delineated a surface area of two leagues square (8,800 acres) centered on the <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%B3calo" title="Zócalo">Zocalo</a>. This area was then separated from the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Mexico" title="State of Mexico">State of Mexico</a>, forcing that state's government to move from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palace_of_the_Inquisition_(Museum_of_Mexican_Medicine)" title="Palace of the Inquisition (Museum of Mexican Medicine)">Palace of the Inquisition (now Museum of Mexican Medicine)</a> in the city to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Texcoco,_Mexico_State" title="Texcoco, Mexico State">Texcoco</a>. This area did not include the population centers of the towns of <a href="/wiki/Coyoac%C3%A1n" title="Coyoacán">Coyoacán</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xochimilco" title="Xochimilco">Xochimilco</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Mateo_Mexicaltzingo" title="San Mateo Mexicaltzingo">Mexicaltzingo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tlalpan" title="Tlalpan">Tlalpan</a>, all of which remained as part of the State of Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EncMex2003_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-EncMex2003-132">[131]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1854 president <a href="/wiki/Antonio_L%C3%B3pez_de_Santa_Anna" title="Antonio López de Santa Anna">Antonio López de Santa Anna</a> enlarged the area of Mexico City almost eightfold from the original 220 to 1,700 km<sup>2</sup> (80 to 660 sq mi), annexing the rural and mountainous areas to secure the strategic mountain passes to the south and southwest to protect the city in event of a foreign invasion. (The <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican–American War">Mexican–American War</a> had just been fought.) The last changes to the limits of Mexico City were made between 1898 and 1902, reducing the area to the current 1,479 km<sup>2</sup> (571 sq mi) by adjusting the southern border with the state of <a href="/wiki/Morelos" title="Morelos">Morelos</a>. By that time, the total number of municipalities within Mexico City was twenty-two. In 1941, the <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Mar%C3%ADa_de_Anaya" title="Pedro María de Anaya">General Anaya</a> borough was merged with the Central Department, which was then renamed "Mexico City" (thus reviving the name but not the autonomous municipality). From 1941 to 1970, the Federal District comprised twelve <i>delegaciones</i> and Mexico City. In 1970, Mexico City was split into four different <i>delegaciones</i>: <a href="/wiki/Cuauht%C3%A9moc,_Mexico_City" title="Cuauhtémoc, Mexico City">Cuauhtémoc</a>, <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Hidalgo,_Mexico_City" title="Miguel Hidalgo, Mexico City">Miguel Hidalgo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Venustiano_Carranza,_Mexico_City" title="Venustiano Carranza, Mexico City">Venustiano Carranza</a> and <a href="/wiki/Benito_Ju%C3%A1rez,_Mexico_City" title="Benito Juárez, Mexico City">Benito Juárez</a>, increasing the number of <i>delegaciones</i> to 16. Since then, the whole Federal District, whose <i>delegaciones</i> had by then almost formed a single urban area, began to be considered <i>de facto</i> a synonym of Mexico City.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-df.gob.mx_133-0"><a href="#cite_note-df.gob.mx-133">[132]</a></sup>
</p><p>The lack of a <i>de jure</i> stipulation left a legal vacuum that led to a number of sterile discussions about whether one concept had engulfed the other or if the latter had ceased to exist altogether. In 1993, the situation was solved by an amendment to the 44th article of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Mexico" title="Constitution of Mexico">Constitution of Mexico</a>; Mexico City and the Federal District were stated to be the same entity. The amendment was later introduced into the second article of the Statute of Government of the Federal District.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-df.gob.mx_133-1"><a href="#cite_note-df.gob.mx-133">[132]</a></sup>
</p><p>On 29 January 2016, Mexico City ceased to be the <i>Federal District</i> (Spanish: <i>Distrito Federal</i> or D.F.), and was officially renamed "Ciudad de México" (or "CDMX").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Federal_District_Now_Officially_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Federal_District_Now_Officially-26">[25]</a></sup> On that date, Mexico City began a transition to becoming the country's 32nd federal entity, giving it a level of autonomy comparable to that of a state. It will have its own constitution and its legislature, and its <i>delegaciones</i> will now be headed by mayors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Federal_District_Now_Officially_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-Federal_District_Now_Officially-26">[25]</a></sup> Because of a clause in the Mexican Constitution, however, as it is the seat of the powers of the federation, it can never become a state, or the capital of the country has to be relocated elsewhere.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UN2_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-UN2-28">[27]</a></sup>
</p><p>In response to the demands, Mexico City received a greater degree of autonomy, with the 1987 elaboration the first Statute of Government (<i>Estatuto de Gobierno</i>) and the creation of an assembly of representatives.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Pages: 149–150">: 149–150 </span></sup> The city has a Statute of Government, and as of its ratification on 31 January 2017, a <a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Constituci%C3%B3n_Pol%C3%ADtica_de_la_Ciudad_de_M%C3%A9xico" title="es:Constitución Política de la Ciudad de México">constitution</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> similar to the states of the Union. As part of the recent changes in autonomy, the budget is administered locally; it is proposed by the head of government and approved by the Legislative Assembly. Nonetheless, it is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Congress_of_Mexico" title="Congress of Mexico">Congress of the Union</a> that sets the ceiling to internal and external <a href="/wiki/Government_debt" title="Government debt">public debt</a> issued by the city government.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup>
</p><p>The politics pursued by the administrations of heads of government in Mexico City at the end of the 20th century have usually been more liberal than those of the rest of the country,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup> whether with the support of the federal government, as was the case with the approval of several comprehensive environmental laws in the 1980s, or by laws that were since approved by the Legislative Assembly. The Legislative Assembly expanded provisions on abortions, becoming the first federal entity to expand <a href="/wiki/Abortion_in_Mexico" title="Abortion in Mexico">abortion in Mexico</a> beyond cases of rape and economic reasons, to permit it at the choice of the mother before the 12th week of pregnancy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup> In December 2009, the then Federal District became the first city in Latin America and one of very few in the world to legalize <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage" title="Same-sex marriage">same-sex marriage</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Boroughs_and_neighborhoods">Boroughs and neighborhoods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Boroughs and neighborhoods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Boroughs_of_Mexico_City" title="Boroughs of Mexico City">Boroughs of Mexico City</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_neighborhoods_in_Mexico_City" title="List of neighborhoods in Mexico City">Neighborhoods in Mexico City</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Boroughs_of_Mexican_Federal_District_numbered.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="717" data-file-width="536" decoding="async" height="294" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Boroughs_of_Mexican_Federal_District_numbered.svg/220px-Boroughs_of_Mexican_Federal_District_numbered.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Boroughs_of_Mexican_Federal_District_numbered.svg/330px-Boroughs_of_Mexican_Federal_District_numbered.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/Boroughs_of_Mexican_Federal_District_numbered.svg/440px-Boroughs_of_Mexican_Federal_District_numbered.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Boroughs_of_Mexican_Federal_District_numbered.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The 16 boroughs of Mexico City</div></div></div>
<p>After the political reforms on 2016, the city is divided for administrative purposes into 16 boroughs (<i>demarcaciones territoriales</i>, colloquially <i>alcaldías</i>), formerly called <i>delegaciones</i>. While they are not fully equivalent to municipalities, the boroughs have gained significant autonomy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cdmxconst_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-cdmxconst-142">[141]</a></sup> Formerly appointed by the Federal District's head of government, local authorities were first elected directly by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plurality_voting_system" title="Plurality voting system">plurality</a> in 2000. From 2016, each borough is headed by a mayor, expanding their local government powers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cdmxconst_142-1"><a href="#cite_note-cdmxconst-142">[141]</a></sup>
</p><p>The boroughs of Mexico City with their 2020 populations are:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-census2020_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-census2020-143">[142]</a></sup>
</p>
<table cellspacing="8">
<tbody><tr>
<td style="width:50%;">
<p>1. <a href="/wiki/%C3%81lvaro_Obreg%C3%B3n,_Mexico_City" title="Álvaro Obregón, Mexico City">Álvaro Obregón</a> (pop. 759,137)<br/>
2. <a href="/wiki/Azcapotzalco" title="Azcapotzalco">Azcapotzalco</a> (pop. 432,205)<br/>
3. <a href="/wiki/Benito_Ju%C3%A1rez,_Mexico_City" title="Benito Juárez, Mexico City">Benito Juárez</a> (pop. 434,153)<br/>
4. <a href="/wiki/Coyoac%C3%A1n" title="Coyoacán">Coyoacán</a> (pop. 614,447)<br/>
5. <a href="/wiki/Cuajimalpa" title="Cuajimalpa">Cuajimalpa</a> (pop. 217,686)<br/>
6. <a href="/wiki/Cuauht%C3%A9moc,_Mexico_City" title="Cuauhtémoc, Mexico City">Cuauhtémoc</a> (pop. 545,884)<br/>
7. <a href="/wiki/Gustavo_A._Madero,_Mexico_City" title="Gustavo A. Madero, Mexico City">Gustavo A. Madero</a> (pop. 1,173,351)<br/>
8. <a href="/wiki/Iztacalco" title="Iztacalco">Iztacalco</a> (pop. 404,695)
</p>
</td>
<td style="width:33%;">
<p>9. <a href="/wiki/Iztapalapa" title="Iztapalapa">Iztapalapa</a> (pop. 1,835,486)<br/>
10. <a href="/wiki/Magdalena_Contreras" title="Magdalena Contreras">La Magdalena Contreras</a> (pop. 247,622)<br/>
11. <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Hidalgo,_Mexico_City" title="Miguel Hidalgo, Mexico City">Miguel Hidalgo</a> (pop. 414,470)<br/>
12. <a href="/wiki/Milpa_Alta" title="Milpa Alta">Milpa Alta</a> (pop. 152,685)<br/>
13. <a href="/wiki/Tl%C3%A1huac" title="Tláhuac">Tláhuac</a> (pop. 392,313)<br/>
14. <a href="/wiki/Tlalpan" title="Tlalpan">Tlalpan</a> (pop. 699,928)<br/>
15. <a href="/wiki/Venustiano_Carranza,_Mexico_City" title="Venustiano Carranza, Mexico City">Venustiano Carranza</a> (pop. 443,704)<br/>
16. <a href="/wiki/Xochimilco" title="Xochimilco">Xochimilco</a> (pop. 442,178)
</p>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> report of 2005<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DISTRITO_FEDERAL_144-0"><a href="#cite_note-DISTRITO_FEDERAL-144">[143]</a></sup> shows that there were three boroughs with a very high Human Development Index, 12 with a high HDI value (9 above .85), and one with a medium HDI value (almost high). <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Benito_Juarez,_Mexico_City" title="Benito Juarez, Mexico City">Benito Juárez</a> borough had the highest HDI of the country (0.9510) followed by <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Hidalgo,_Mexico_City" title="Miguel Hidalgo, Mexico City">Miguel Hidalgo</a>, which came up fourth nationally with an HDI of (0.9189), and <a href="/wiki/Coyoac%C3%A1n" title="Coyoacán">Coyoacán</a> was fifth nationally, with an HDI of (0.9169). <a href="/wiki/Cuajimalpa" title="Cuajimalpa">Cuajimalpa</a> (15th), <a href="/wiki/Cuauht%C3%A9moc,_Mexico_City" title="Cuauhtémoc, Mexico City">Cuauhtémoc</a> (23rd), and <a href="/wiki/Azcapotzalco" title="Azcapotzalco">Azcapotzalco</a> (25th) also had very high values of 0.8994, 0.8922, and 0.8915, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DISTRITO_FEDERAL_144-1"><a href="#cite_note-DISTRITO_FEDERAL-144">[143]</a></sup>
</p><p>In contrast, the boroughs of <a href="/wiki/Xochimilco" title="Xochimilco">Xochimilco</a> (172nd), <a href="/wiki/Tl%C3%A1huac" title="Tláhuac">Tláhuac</a> (177th), and <a href="/wiki/Iztapalapa" title="Iztapalapa">Iztapalapa</a> (183rd) presented the lowest HDI values of Mexico City, with values of 0.8481, 0.8473, and 0.8464, respectively, which are still in the global high-HDI range. The only borough that did not have a high HDI was that of rural <a href="/wiki/Milpa_Alta" title="Milpa Alta">Milpa Alta</a>, which had a "medium" HDI of 0.7984, far below those of all the other boroughs (627th nationally, the rest being in the top 200). Mexico City's HDI for the 2005 report was 0.9012 (very high), and its 2010 value of 0.9225 (very high), or (by newer methodology) 0.8307, was Mexico's highest.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DISTRITO_FEDERAL_144-2"><a href="#cite_note-DISTRITO_FEDERAL-144">[143]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_enforcement">Law enforcement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Law enforcement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Law_enforcement_in_Mexico_City" title="Law enforcement in Mexico City">Law enforcement in Mexico City</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FederalPoliceDF.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="576" decoding="async" height="302" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/FederalPoliceDF.jpg/170px-FederalPoliceDF.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/FederalPoliceDF.jpg/255px-FederalPoliceDF.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/FederalPoliceDF.jpg/340px-FederalPoliceDF.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FederalPoliceDF.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Federal_Police_(Mexico)" title="Federal Police (Mexico)">Federal Police</a> headquarters in Mexico City</div></div></div>
<p>The Secretariat of Public Security of Mexico City (Secretaría de Seguridad Pública de la Ciudad de México – SSP) manages a combined force of over 90,000 officers in Mexico City. The SSP is charged with maintaining <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_order_crime" title="Public order crime">public order</a> and safety in the heart of Mexico City. The historic district is also roamed by tourist police, aiming to orient and serve tourists. These horse-mounted agents dress in traditional uniforms. The investigative Judicial Police of Mexico City (Policía Judicial de la Ciudad de México – PJCDMX) is organized under the Office of the <a href="/wiki/Attorney_General_of_Mexico" title="Attorney General of Mexico">Attorney General of Mexico</a> City (the Procuraduría General de Justicia de la Ciudad de México). The PGJCDMX maintains 16 precincts (delegaciones) with an estimated 3,500 judicial police, 1,100 investigating agents for prosecuting attorneys (agentes del ministerio público), and nearly 1,000 criminology experts or specialists (peritos).
</p><p>Between 2000 and 2004 an average of 478 crimes were reported each day in Mexico City; however, the actual crime rate is thought to be much higher "since most people are reluctant to report crime".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup> Under policies enacted by Mayor <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_Ebrard" title="Marcelo Ebrard">Marcelo Ebrard</a> between 2009 and 2011, Mexico City underwent a major security upgrade with violent and petty crime rates both falling significantly despite the rise in violent crime in other parts of the country. Some of the policies enacted included the installation of 11,000 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Security_camera" title="Security camera">security cameras</a> around the city and a very large expansion of the police force. Mexico City has one of the world's highest police officer-to-resident ratios, with one uniformed officer per 100 citizens.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup> Since 1997 the prison population has increased by more than 500%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mueller_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-mueller-147">[146]</a></sup> Political scientist Markus-Michael Müller argues that mostly informal street vendors are hit by these measures. He sees punishment "related to the growing politicization of security and crime issues and the resulting criminalization of the people living at the margins of urban society, in particular those who work in the city's informal economy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mueller_147-1"><a href="#cite_note-mueller-147">[146]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, the incidence of <a href="/wiki/Femicide" title="Femicide">femicides</a> was 3.2 per 100 000 inhabitants, the national average being 4.2.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> A 2015 city government report found that two of three women over the age of 15 in the capital suffered some form of violence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup> In addition to <a href="/wiki/Street_harassment" title="Street harassment">street harassment</a>, one of the places where women in Mexico City are subjected to violence is on and around public transport. Annually the Metro of Mexico City receives 300 complaints of <a href="/wiki/Sexual_harassment" title="Sexual harassment">sexual harassment</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup> While the violence against women in Mexico City is rising, there is still a large number of incidents of kidnappings and killings that go undetected and unreported due to the corruption in the police department.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_relations">International relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: International relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Mexico" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Mexico">List of twin towns and sister cities in Mexico</a></div>

</p>

</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sobrevuelos_CDMX_IMG_5982_(39488832615).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1500" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Sobrevuelos_CDMX_IMG_5982_%2839488832615%29.jpg/220px-Sobrevuelos_CDMX_IMG_5982_%2839488832615%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Sobrevuelos_CDMX_IMG_5982_%2839488832615%29.jpg/330px-Sobrevuelos_CDMX_IMG_5982_%2839488832615%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/Sobrevuelos_CDMX_IMG_5982_%2839488832615%29.jpg/440px-Sobrevuelos_CDMX_IMG_5982_%2839488832615%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sobrevuelos_CDMX_IMG_5982_(39488832615).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Paseo_de_la_Reforma" title="Paseo de la Reforma">Paseo de la Reforma</a> is a wide avenue designed by <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_von_Rosenzweig" title="Ferdinand von Rosenzweig">Ferdinand von Rosenzweig</a> in the 1860s and was modeled after the <a href="/wiki/Champs-%C3%89lys%C3%A9es" title="Champs-Élysées">Champs-Élysées</a> in Paris.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arquitectura_del_Parque_la_Mexicana.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3024" data-file-width="4032" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Arquitectura_del_Parque_la_Mexicana.jpg/220px-Arquitectura_del_Parque_la_Mexicana.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Arquitectura_del_Parque_la_Mexicana.jpg/330px-Arquitectura_del_Parque_la_Mexicana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Arquitectura_del_Parque_la_Mexicana.jpg/440px-Arquitectura_del_Parque_la_Mexicana.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arquitectura_del_Parque_la_Mexicana.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe,_Mexico_City" title="Santa Fe, Mexico City">Santa Fe</a> is one of the centers of greatest economic activity in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bolsa_Mexicana_de_Valores_-_panoramio.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3658" data-file-width="3656" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Bolsa_Mexicana_de_Valores_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-Bolsa_Mexicana_de_Valores_-_panoramio.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Bolsa_Mexicana_de_Valores_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-Bolsa_Mexicana_de_Valores_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Bolsa_Mexicana_de_Valores_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-Bolsa_Mexicana_de_Valores_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bolsa_Mexicana_de_Valores_-_panoramio.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mexican_Stock_Exchange" title="Mexican Stock Exchange">Mexican Stock Exchange</a></div></div></div>
<p>Mexico City is one of the most important economic hubs in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>. The city proper produces 15.8% of the country's <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">gross domestic product</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INEGI_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-INEGI-156">[155]</a></sup> In 2002, Mexico City had a <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> score of 0.915,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup> identical to that of <a href="/wiki/International_rankings_of_South_Korea" title="International rankings of South Korea">South Korea</a>. In 2007, residents in the top twelve percent of GDP per capita holders in the city had a mean <a href="/wiki/Disposable_and_discretionary_income" title="Disposable and discretionary income">disposable income</a> of <span style="white-space: nowrap"><a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">US$</a>98,517</span>. The high spending power of Mexico City inhabitants makes the city attractive for companies offering prestige and <a href="/wiki/Luxury_goods" title="Luxury goods">luxury goods</a>. According to a 2009 study conducted by <a href="/wiki/PricewaterhouseCoopers" title="PricewaterhouseCoopers">PwC</a>, Mexico City had a GDP of $390 billion, ranking it as the eighth richest city in the world and the richest in Latin America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ukmediacentre.pwc.com_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-ukmediacentre.pwc.com-158">[157]</a></sup> In 2009, Mexico City alone would rank as the 30th largest economy in the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-emporis_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-emporis-159">[158]</a></sup>
</p><p>Mexico City is the greatest contributor to the country's industrial GDP (15.8%) and also the greatest contributor to the country's GDP in the <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">service sector</a> (25.3%). Due to the limited non-urbanized space at the south—most of which is protected through environmental laws—the contribution of Mexico City in agriculture is the smallest of all federal entities in the country.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-INEGI_156-1"><a href="#cite_note-INEGI-156">[155]</a></sup> The economic reforms of President <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Salinas_de_Gortari" title="Carlos Salinas de Gortari">Carlos Salinas de Gortari</a> had a tremendous effect on the city, as a number of businesses, including banks and airlines, were privatized. He also signed the <a href="/wiki/North_American_Free_Trade_Agreement" title="North American Free Trade Agreement">North American Free Trade Agreement</a> (NAFTA). This led to decentralization<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-furness_160-0"><a href="#cite_note-furness-160">[159]</a></sup> and a shift in Mexico City's economic base, from manufacturing to services, as most factories moved away to either the <a href="/wiki/State_of_Mexico" title="State of Mexico">State of Mexico</a>, or more commonly to the northern border. By contrast, corporate office buildings set their base in the city.
</p><p>Mexico City offers an immense and varied consumer retail market, ranging from basic foods to ultra high-end luxury goods. Consumers may buy in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Traditional_fixed_markets_in_Mexico" title="Traditional fixed markets in Mexico">fixed indoor markets</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Tianguis" title="Tianguis">mobile markets (<i>tianguis</i>)</a>, from <a href="/wiki/Street_vendors_in_Mexico_City" title="Street vendors in Mexico City">street vendors</a>, from downtown shops in a street dedicated to a certain type of good, in convenience stores and traditional neighborhood stores, in modern supermarkets, in warehouse and membership stores and the shopping centers that they anchor, in department stores, in <a href="/wiki/Big-box_store" title="Big-box store">big-box stores</a>, and in modern shopping malls. In addition, "<a href="/wiki/Tianguis" title="Tianguis">tianguis</a>" or mobile markets set up shop on streets in many neighborhoods, depending on day of week. Sundays see the largest number of these markets.
</p><p>The city's main source of fresh produce is the <a href="/wiki/Central_de_Abasto" title="Central de Abasto">Central de Abasto</a>. This in itself is a self-contained mini-city in <a href="/wiki/Iztapalapa" title="Iztapalapa">Iztapalapa</a> borough covering an area equivalent to several dozen city blocks. The wholesale market supplies most of the city's "mercados", supermarkets and restaurants, as well as people who come to buy the produce for themselves. Tons of fresh produce are trucked in from all over Mexico every day. The principal fish market is known as <a href="/wiki/La_Nueva_Viga_Market" title="La Nueva Viga Market">La Nueva Viga</a>, in the same complex as the Central de Abastos.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-actecon_161-0"><a href="#cite_note-actecon-161">[160]</a></sup> The world-renowned market of <a href="/wiki/Tepito" title="Tepito">Tepito</a> occupies 25 blocks, and sells a variety of products. A staple for consumers in the city is the omnipresent "mercado". Every major neighborhood in the city has its own borough-regulated market, often more than one. These are large well-established facilities offering most basic products, such as fresh produce and meat/poultry, dry goods, tortillerías, and many other services such as locksmiths, herbal medicine, hardware goods, sewing implements; and a multitude of stands offering freshly made, home-style cooking and drinks in the tradition of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aguas_frescas" title="Aguas frescas">aguas frescas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atole" title="Atole">atole</a>.
</p><p>Street vendors ply their trade from stalls in the <i>tianguis</i> as well as at non-officially controlled concentrations around metro stations and hospitals; at <i>plazas comerciales</i>, where vendors of a certain "theme" (e.g. stationery) are housed; originally these were organized to accommodate vendors formerly selling on the street; or simply from improvised stalls on a city sidewalk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pena_162-0"><a href="#cite_note-pena-162">[161]</a></sup> In addition, food and goods are sold from people walking with baskets, pushing carts, from bicycles or the backs of trucks, or simply from a tarp or cloth laid on the ground.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[162]</a></sup> In the center of the city informal street vendors are increasingly targeted by laws and prosecution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mueller_147-2"><a href="#cite_note-mueller-147">[146]</a></sup> The weekly <a href="/wiki/San_Felipe_de_Jes%C3%BAs_Tianguis" title="San Felipe de Jesús Tianguis">San Felipe de Jesús Tianguis</a> is reported to be the largest in Latin America.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[163]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Historic_Center_of_Mexico_City" title="Historic Center of Mexico City">Historic Center of Mexico City</a> is widely known for specialized, often low-cost retailers. Certain blocks or streets are dedicated to shops selling a certain type of merchandise, with areas dedicated to over 40 categories such as home appliances, lamps and electricals, closets and bathrooms, housewares, wedding dresses, jukeboxes, printing, office furniture and safes, books, photography, jewelry, and opticians.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Barrios_M%C3%A1gicos_of_Mexico_City" title="Barrios Mágicos of Mexico City">Barrios Mágicos of Mexico City</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Turibus_Ciudad_de_Mexico.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="499" decoding="async" height="245" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Turibus_Ciudad_de_Mexico.jpg/170px-Turibus_Ciudad_de_Mexico.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Turibus_Ciudad_de_Mexico.jpg/255px-Turibus_Ciudad_de_Mexico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Turibus_Ciudad_de_Mexico.jpg/340px-Turibus_Ciudad_de_Mexico.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Turibus_Ciudad_de_Mexico.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Turibus runs through many of the most important tourist attractions in the city.</div></div></div>
<p>Mexico City is a destination for many foreign tourists. The <a href="/wiki/Historic_center_of_Mexico_City" title="Historic center of Mexico City">Historic center of Mexico City</a> (<i>Centro Histórico</i>) and the "floating gardens" of <a href="/wiki/Xochimilco" title="Xochimilco">Xochimilco</a> in the southern borough have been declared <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a> by <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>. Landmarks in the Historic Center include the <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%B3calo" title="Zócalo">Plaza de la Constitución</a> (Zócalo), the main central square with its epoch-contrasting Spanish-era <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_Metropolitan_Cathedral" title="Mexico City Metropolitan Cathedral">Metropolitan Cathedral</a> and <a href="/wiki/National_Palace_(Mexico)" title="National Palace (Mexico)">National Palace</a>, ancient Aztec temple ruins <a href="/wiki/Templo_Mayor" title="Templo Mayor">Templo Mayor</a> ("Major Temple") and modern structures, all within a few steps of one another. (The Templo Mayor was discovered in 1978 while workers were digging to place underground electric cables).
</p><p>The most recognizable icon of Mexico City is the golden <a href="/wiki/Angel_of_Independence" title="Angel of Independence">Angel of Independence</a> on the wide, elegant avenue <a href="/wiki/Paseo_de_la_Reforma" title="Paseo de la Reforma">Paseo de la Reforma</a>, modeled by the order of the Emperor <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_I_of_Mexico" title="Maximilian I of Mexico">Maximilian of Mexico</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Champs-%C3%89lys%C3%A9es" title="Champs-Élysées">Champs-Élysées</a> in Paris. This avenue was designed over the Americas' oldest known major roadway in the 19th century to connect the <a href="/wiki/National_Palace_(Mexico)" title="National Palace (Mexico)">National Palace</a> (seat of government) with the <a href="/wiki/Chapultepec_Castle" title="Chapultepec Castle">Castle of Chapultepec</a>, the imperial residence. Today, this avenue is an important financial district in which the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Stock_Exchange" title="Mexican Stock Exchange">Mexican Stock Exchange</a> and several <a href="/wiki/Corporate_headquarters" title="Corporate headquarters">corporate headquarters</a> are located. Another important avenue is the <a href="/wiki/Avenida_de_los_Insurgentes" title="Avenida de los Insurgentes">Avenida de los Insurgentes</a>, which extends 28.8 km (17.9 mi) and is one of the longest single avenues in the world.
