</p><p><a href="/wiki/Chapultepec" title="Chapultepec">Chapultepec</a> Park houses the <a href="/wiki/Chapultepec_Castle" title="Chapultepec Castle">Chapultepec Castle</a>, now a museum on a hill that overlooks the park and its numerous museums, monuments and the national zoo and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Museo_Nacional_de_Antropolog%C3%ADa" title="Museo Nacional de Antropología">National Museum of Anthropology</a> (which houses the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aztec_calendar_stone" title="Aztec calendar stone">Aztec Calendar Stone</a>). Another piece of architecture is the <a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_Bellas_Artes" title="Palacio de Bellas Artes">Palacio de Bellas Artes</a>, a white marble theater/museum whose weight is such that it has gradually been sinking into the soft ground below. Its construction began during the presidency of <a href="/wiki/Porfirio_D%C3%ADaz" title="Porfirio Díaz">Porfirio Díaz</a> and ended in 1934, after being interrupted by the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Revolution" title="Mexican Revolution">Mexican Revolution</a> in the 1920s. The <a href="/wiki/Plaza_de_las_Tres_Culturas" title="Plaza de las Tres Culturas">Plaza de las Tres Culturas</a>, in this square are located the <a href="/wiki/Colegio_de_Santa_Cruz_de_Tlatelolco" title="Colegio de Santa Cruz de Tlatelolco">College of Santa Cruz de Tlatelolco</a>, that is <a href="/wiki/List_of_oldest_buildings_in_the_Americas" title="List of oldest buildings in the Americas">the first and oldest</a> European school of higher learning in the <a href="/wiki/Americas" title="Americas">Americas</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-catalog.hathitrust.org_125-1"><a href="#cite_note-catalog.hathitrust.org-125">[124]</a></sup> and the archeological site of the <a href="/wiki/Tlatelolco_(archaeological_site)" title="Tlatelolco (archaeological site)">city-state of Tlatelolco</a>, and the shrine and <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_Our_Lady_of_Guadalupe" title="Basilica of Our Lady of Guadalupe">Basilica of Our Lady of Guadalupe</a> are also important sites. There is a <a href="/wiki/Double-decker_bus" title="Double-decker bus">double-decker bus</a>, known as the "Turibus", that circles most of these sites, and has timed audio describing the sites in multiple languages as they are passed.
</p><p>In addition, according to the Secretariat of Tourism, the city has about 170 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Museums" title="Museums">museums</a>—is among the top ten of cities in the world with highest number of museums<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[166]</a></sup>—over 100 <a href="/wiki/Art_museum" title="Art museum">art galleries</a>, and some 30 <a href="/wiki/List_of_concert_halls" title="List of concert halls">concert halls</a>, all of which maintain a constant cultural activity during the whole year. Many areas (e.g. Palacio Nacional and the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=National_Institute_of_Cardiology&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="National Institute of Cardiology (page does not exist)">National Institute of Cardiology</a>) have murals painted by <a href="/wiki/Diego_Rivera" title="Diego Rivera">Diego Rivera</a>. He and his wife <a href="/wiki/Frida_Kahlo" title="Frida Kahlo">Frida Kahlo</a> lived in <a href="/wiki/Coyoac%C3%A1n" title="Coyoacán">Coyoacán</a>, where several of their homes, studios, and art collections are open to the public. The house where <a href="/wiki/Leon_Trotsky" title="Leon Trotsky">Leon Trotsky</a> was initially granted asylum and finally murdered in 1940 is also in Coyoacán. In addition, there are several <i><a href="/wiki/Hacienda" title="Hacienda">haciendas</a></i> that are now restaurants, such as the San Ángel Inn, the Hacienda de Tlalpan, Hacienda de Cortés and the Hacienda de los Morales.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airports">Airports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Airports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:AICM_AIR_T2.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="553" data-file-width="777" decoding="async" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/AICM_AIR_T2.jpg/220px-AICM_AIR_T2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/AICM_AIR_T2.jpg/330px-AICM_AIR_T2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/AICM_AIR_T2.jpg/440px-AICM_AIR_T2.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:AICM_AIR_T2.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_International_Airport" title="Mexico City International Airport">Mexico City International Airport</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_International_Airport" title="Mexico City International Airport">Mexico City International Airport</a> is Mexico City's primary airport (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">IATA Airport Code</a>: MEX). This airport is Latin America's <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Latin_America" title="List of the busiest airports in Latin America">busiest</a>, with daily flights to United States and Canada, Mexico, Central America and the Caribbean, South America, Europe and Asia. <a href="/wiki/Aerom%C3%A9xico" title="Aeroméxico">Aeroméxico</a> (<a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">Skyteam</a>) is based at this airport, and has codeshare agreements with non-Mexican airlines that span the entire globe. The airport is also a hub for <a href="/wiki/Volaris" title="Volaris">Volaris</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VivaAerobus" title="VivaAerobus">VivaAerobus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aeromar" title="Aeromar">Aeromar</a>. It was a hub for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexicana_de_Aviacion" title="Mexicana de Aviacion">Mexicana de Aviacion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Interjet" title="Interjet">Interjet</a> in the past.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Felipe_%C3%81ngeles_International_Airport" title="Felipe Ángeles International Airport">Felipe Ángeles International Airport</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">IATA Airport Code</a>: NLU) is Mexico City's secondary airport. The airport opened in 2022, rebuilt from the former Santa Lucía Air Force Base. It is located in <a href="/wiki/Zumpango" title="Zumpango">Zumpango</a>, <a href="/wiki/State_of_Mexico" title="State of Mexico">State of Mexico</a>, 48.8 kilometres (30 mi) north-northeast of the <a href="/wiki/Historic_center_of_Mexico_City" title="Historic center of Mexico City">historic center of Mexico City</a> by car.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[167]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[168]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transportation">Public transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Public transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Mexico City has many modes of public transportation, from the <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_Metro" title="Mexico City Metro">metro</a> (subway) system, to <a href="/wiki/Tren_Suburbano" title="Tren Suburbano">suburban rail</a>, <a href="/wiki/Xochimilco_Light_Rail" title="Xochimilco Light Rail">light rail</a>, regular buses and minibusses (locally known as "<i><a href="/wiki/Pesero" title="Pesero">peseros</a></i>"), <a href="/wiki/Bus_rapid_transit" title="Bus rapid transit">bus rapid transit</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_Metrob%C3%BAs" title="Mexico City Metrobús">Metrobús</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mexib%C3%BAs" title="Mexibús">Mexibús</a>—partially—systems), and <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Mexico_City" title="Trolleybuses in Mexico City">trolleybuses</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Ecobici_(Mexico_City)" title="Ecobici (Mexico City)">bike share</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cableb%C3%BAs" title="Cablebús">cableways</a>. In 2019, the graphic designer <a href="/wiki/Lance_Wyman" title="Lance Wyman">Lance Wyman</a> was engaged to create an integrated map of the multimodal public transportation system; he presented a new logo for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Movilidad_Integrada" title="Movilidad Integrada">Sistema de Movilidad Integrada</a>, describing eight distinct modes of transportation. The head of the government, <a href="/wiki/Claudia_Sheinbaum" title="Claudia Sheinbaum">Claudia Sheinbaum</a>, said the branding would be used for a new single payment card to streamline public transportation fare collection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[169]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_Metro" title="Mexico City Metro">Mexico City Metro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tren_Suburbano" title="Tren Suburbano">Tren Suburbano</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FE-10_06.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2460" data-file-width="3280" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/FE-10_06.jpg/220px-FE-10_06.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/FE-10_06.jpg/330px-FE-10_06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/FE-10_06.jpg/440px-FE-10_06.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FE-10_06.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_Metro" title="Mexico City Metro">Mexico City Metro</a></div></div></div>
<p>Mexico City is served by the <i><a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_Metro" title="Mexico City Metro">Sistema de Transporte Colectivo</a></i>, a 225.9 km (140 mi) <a href="/wiki/Rapid_transit" title="Rapid transit">metro</a> system, which is the largest in Latin America. The first portions were opened in 1969 and it has expanded to 12 lines with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Mexico_City_metro_stations" title="List of Mexico City metro stations">195 stations</a>. The metro transports 4.4 million people every day. It is the 8th busiest metro system in the world, behind Tokyo (10.0 million), Beijing (9.3 million), Shanghai (7.8 million), Seoul (7.3 million), Moscow (6.7 million), Guangzhou (6.2 million), and New York City (4.9 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[170]</a></sup> It is heavily subsidized, and has some of the lowest fares in the world, each trip costing 5.00 <a href="/wiki/Mexican_peso" title="Mexican peso">pesos</a> (roughly US$0.27) from 05:00 am to midnight. Several stations display <a href="/wiki/Pre-Columbian_era" title="Pre-Columbian era">pre-Columbian</a> artifacts and architecture that were discovered during the metro's construction.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> However, the metro covers less than half of the total urban area. The Metro stations are also differentiated by the use of icons and glyphs which were created for the illiterate, a unique system that has become iconic characteristic of Mexico City. Each icon was developed based on historical (characters, sites, pre-Hispanic motifs), linguistic, symbolic (glyphs) or geographic references. A complementary system of icons was used for the Metrobús (BRT) stops.
</p><p>A suburban rail system, the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ferrocarril_Suburbano_de_la_Zona_Metropolitana_del_Valle_de_M%C3%A9xico" title="Ferrocarril Suburbano de la Zona Metropolitana del Valle de México">Tren Suburbano</a></i> serves the metropolitan area, beyond the reach of the <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_Metro" title="Mexico City Metro">metro</a>, with only one line serving to municipalities such as <a href="/wiki/Tlalnepantla_de_Baz" title="Tlalnepantla de Baz">Tlalnepantla</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuautitl%C3%A1n_Izcalli,_Mexico_State" title="Cuautitlán Izcalli, Mexico State">Cuautitlán Izcalli</a>, but with future lines planned to serve e.g. <a href="/wiki/Chalco_de_D%C3%ADaz_Covarrubias" title="Chalco de Díaz Covarrubias">Chalco</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Reyes_Acaquilpan" title="Los Reyes Acaquilpan">La Paz</a>.
</p><p>Electric transport other than the metro also exists, in the form of several <a href="/wiki/Trolleybuses_in_Mexico_City" title="Trolleybuses in Mexico City">Mexico City trolleybus</a> routes and the <a href="/wiki/Xochimilco_Light_Rail" title="Xochimilco Light Rail">Xochimilco Light Rail</a> line, both of which are operated by <a href="/wiki/Servicio_de_Transportes_El%C3%A9ctricos" title="Servicio de Transportes Eléctricos">Servicio de Transportes Eléctricos</a>. The central area's last <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">streetcar</a> line (tramway, or <i><a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tranv%C3%ADa" title="es:Tranvía">tranvía</a></i>) closed in 1979.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_Metrob%C3%BAs" title="Mexico City Metrobús">Mexico City Metrobús</a> and <a href="/wiki/Red_de_Transporte_de_Pasajeros" title="Red de Transporte de Pasajeros">Red de Transporte de Pasajeros</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:15-07-17-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-WMA_1274.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4016" data-file-width="6016" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/15-07-17-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-WMA_1274.jpg/220px-15-07-17-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-WMA_1274.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/15-07-17-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-WMA_1274.jpg/330px-15-07-17-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-WMA_1274.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/15-07-17-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-WMA_1274.jpg/440px-15-07-17-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-WMA_1274.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:15-07-17-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-WMA_1274.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_Metrob%C3%BAs" title="Mexico City Metrobús">Metrobús</a> rapid transit bus stop station at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mina_(Mexico_City_Metrob%C3%BAs)" title="Mina (Mexico City Metrobús)">Mina</a></div></div></div>
<p>The city's first <a href="/wiki/Bus_rapid_transit" title="Bus rapid transit">bus rapid transit</a> line, the <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_Metrob%C3%BAs" title="Mexico City Metrobús">Metrobús</a>, began operation in June 2005, along <a href="/wiki/Avenida_de_los_Insurgentes" title="Avenida de los Insurgentes">Avenida Insurgentes</a>. More and more lines opened and as of mid-2017 there are 6 routes with a 7th planned along <a href="/wiki/Paseo_de_la_Reforma" title="Paseo de la Reforma">Paseo de la Reforma</a> to connect <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe,_Mexico_City" title="Santa Fe, Mexico City">Santa Fe</a> with the city center and points north.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup> As each line opened, the 'pesero' minibuses were removed from each route, in order to reduce pollution and commute times. As of mid-2017, there were 568<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[172]</a></sup> Metrobús buses. In late 2016 they transported an average of 1.1 million passengers daily.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[173]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mexib%C3%BAs" title="Mexibús">Mexibús</a> provides 3 bus rapid transit lines connecting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metro_Ciudad_Azteca" title="Metro Ciudad Azteca">Metro Ciudad Azteca</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metro_Pantitl%C3%A1n" title="Metro Pantitlán">Metro Pantitlán</a> with <a href="/wiki/Cuautitl%C3%A1n" title="Cuautitlán">Cuautitlán</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ecatepec" title="Ecatepec">Ecatepec</a> and other suburban areas in the State of Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[174]</a></sup>
</p><p>The city has four major bus stations (North, South, Observatorio, TAPO), which comprise one of the world's largest transportation agglomerations, with bus service to many cities across the country and international connections. There are some intercity buses that leave directly from the <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_International_Airport" title="Mexico City International Airport">Mexico City International Airport</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:15-07-20-Bus_in_Mexico_DF-RalfR-N3S_9606.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2508" data-file-width="3262" decoding="async" height="169" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/15-07-20-Bus_in_Mexico_DF-RalfR-N3S_9606.jpg/220px-15-07-20-Bus_in_Mexico_DF-RalfR-N3S_9606.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/15-07-20-Bus_in_Mexico_DF-RalfR-N3S_9606.jpg/330px-15-07-20-Bus_in_Mexico_DF-RalfR-N3S_9606.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/15-07-20-Bus_in_Mexico_DF-RalfR-N3S_9606.jpg/440px-15-07-20-Bus_in_Mexico_DF-RalfR-N3S_9606.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:15-07-20-Bus_in_Mexico_DF-RalfR-N3S_9606.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <i><a href="/wiki/Pesero" title="Pesero">pesero</a></i> or microbús</div></div></div>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Pesero" title="Pesero">peseros</a></i> are typically half-length passenger buses (known as <i>microbús</i>) that sit 22 passengers and stand up to 28. As of 2007<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the approximately 28,000 peseros carried up to 60 percent of the city's passengers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[175]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[176]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[177]</a></sup> In August 2016, Mayor Mancera announced that new pesero vehicle and concessions would be eliminated completely unless they were ecologically friendly vehicles,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[178]</a></sup> and in October 2011 the city's Secretary of Mobility Héctor Serrano states that by the end of the current administration (2018) there would no longer by any peseros/microbuses circulating at all, and that new full-sized buses would take over the routes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-excelsior-pesero_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-excelsior-pesero-180">[179]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, the city launched so-called "Bus Rapid Service", with mid-sized <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz" title="Mercedes-Benz">Mercedes-Benz</a> Boxer buses carrying 75–85 passengers<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[180]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[181]</a></sup> painted purple-on-white, replacing 'peseros' on certain groups of routes. Operation is a concession to the private firms (SAUSA, COTOBUSA, TREPSA) instead of to individual vehicle operators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[182]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[183]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[184]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[185]</a></sup>
</p><p>City agency <a href="/wiki/Red_de_Transporte_de_Pasajeros" title="Red de Transporte de Pasajeros">Red de Transporte de Pasajeros</a> (RTP), formerly M1,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[186]</a></sup> operates various networks of large buses including regular, Ecobús, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Circuito_Bicentenario&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Circuito Bicentenario (page does not exist)">Circuito Bicentenario</a>, Atenea, Express, school and night routes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[187]</a></sup> In 2016, more bus routes were added to replace pesero routes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-excelsior-pesero_180-1"><a href="#cite_note-excelsior-pesero-180">[179]</a></sup> In 2016, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=SVBUS&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="SVBUS (page does not exist)">SVBUS</a> express bus service was launched, with limited stops and utilizing the city's toll roads on the second-level of the <a href="/wiki/Anillo_Perif%C3%A9rico" title="Anillo Periférico">Periférico</a> ring road and <a href="/wiki/Superv%C3%ADa_Poniente" title="Supervía Poniente">Supervía Poniente</a> and connecting <a href="/wiki/Toreo_Parque_Central" title="Toreo Parque Central">Toreo</a>/<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Metro_Cuatro_Caminos" title="Metro Cuatro Caminos">Cuatro Caminos</a> with <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe,_Mexico_City" title="Santa Fe, Mexico City">Santa Fe</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_Jer%C3%B3nimo_L%C3%ADdice" title="San Jerónimo Lídice">San Jerónimo Lídice</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santa_Mar%C3%ADa_Tepepan" title="Santa María Tepepan">Tepepan</a> near <a href="/wiki/Xochimilco" title="Xochimilco">Xochimilco</a> in the southeast. Suburban buses also leave from the city's main intercity bus stations.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads_and_car_transport">Roads and car transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Roads and car transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vista_de_la_Ciudad_de_M%C3%A9xico_desde_Periferico_y_Paseo_de_la_Reforma.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1936" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Vista_de_la_Ciudad_de_M%C3%A9xico_desde_Periferico_y_Paseo_de_la_Reforma.JPG/220px-Vista_de_la_Ciudad_de_M%C3%A9xico_desde_Periferico_y_Paseo_de_la_Reforma.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Vista_de_la_Ciudad_de_M%C3%A9xico_desde_Periferico_y_Paseo_de_la_Reforma.JPG/330px-Vista_de_la_Ciudad_de_M%C3%A9xico_desde_Periferico_y_Paseo_de_la_Reforma.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Vista_de_la_Ciudad_de_M%C3%A9xico_desde_Periferico_y_Paseo_de_la_Reforma.JPG/440px-Vista_de_la_Ciudad_de_M%C3%A9xico_desde_Periferico_y_Paseo_de_la_Reforma.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vista_de_la_Ciudad_de_M%C3%A9xico_desde_Periferico_y_Paseo_de_la_Reforma.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Anillo_Perif%C3%A9rico" title="Anillo Periférico">Anillo Periférico</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paseo_de_la_Reforma" title="Paseo de la Reforma">Paseo de la Reforma</a> in <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Hidalgo,_Mexico_City" title="Miguel Hidalgo, Mexico City">Miguel Hidalgo</a></div></div></div>
<p>In the late 1970s many arterial roads were redesigned as <i><a href="/wiki/Eje_vial" title="Eje vial">ejes viales</a></i>; high-volume one-way roads that cross, in theory, Mexico City proper from side to side. The <i>eje vial</i> network is based on a quasi-<a href="/wiki/Cartesian_coordinate_system" title="Cartesian coordinate system">Cartesian</a> grid, with the <i>ejes</i> themselves being called <i>Eje 1 Poniente</i>, <i>Eje Central</i>, and <i>Eje 1 Oriente</i>, for example, for the north–south roads, and <i>Eje 2 Sur</i> and <i>Eje 3 Norte</i>, for example, for east–west roads. Ring roads are the <a href="/wiki/Circuito_Interior" title="Circuito Interior">Circuito Interior</a> (inner ring), <a href="/wiki/Anillo_Perif%C3%A9rico" title="Anillo Periférico">Anillo Periférico</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Circuito_Exterior_Mexiquense" title="Circuito Exterior Mexiquense">Circuito Exterior Mexiquense</a> ("State of Mexico outer loop") toll road skirting the northeastern and eastern edges of the metropolitan area,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[188]</a></sup> the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Autopista_Chamapa-La_Venta" title="Autopista Chamapa-La Venta">Chamapa-La Venta</a> toll road skirting the northwestern edge, and the <a href="/wiki/Arco_Norte" title="Arco Norte">Arco Norte</a> completely bypassing the metropolitan area in an arc from northwest (<a href="/wiki/Atlacomulco" title="Atlacomulco">Atlacomulco</a>) to north (<a href="/wiki/Tula_de_Allende" title="Tula de Allende">Tula, Hidalgo</a>) to east (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Puebla,_Puebla" title="Puebla, Puebla">Puebla</a>). A second level (where tolls are charged) of the Periférico, colloquially called the <i>segundo piso</i> ("second floor"), was officially opened in 2012, with sections still being completed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[189]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Viaducto_Miguel_Alem%C3%A1n" title="Viaducto Miguel Alemán">Viaducto Miguel Alemán</a> crosses the city east–west from Observatorio to the airport. In 2013 the <a href="/wiki/Superv%C3%ADa_Poniente" title="Supervía Poniente">Supervía Poniente</a> opened, a toll road linking the new <a href="/wiki/Santa_Fe,_Mexico_City" title="Santa Fe, Mexico City">Santa Fe</a> business district with southwestern Mexico City.
</p><p>There is an environmental program, called <a href="/wiki/Hoy_No_Circula" title="Hoy No Circula">Hoy No Circula</a> ("Today Does Not Run", or "One Day without a Car"), whereby vehicles that have not passed emissions testing are restricted from circulating on certain days according to the ending digit of their <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_registration_plate" title="Vehicle registration plate">license plates</a>; this in an attempt to cut down on pollution and traffic congestion. While in 2003, the program still restricted 40% of vehicles in the metropolitan area,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[190]</a></sup> with the adoption of stricter emissions standards in 2001 and 2006,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[191]</a></sup> in practice, these days most vehicles are exempt from the circulation restrictions as long as they pass regular emissions tests.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-193"><a href="#cite_note-193">[192]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Parking">Parking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Parking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Parking_in_Mexico_City" title="Parking in Mexico City">Parking in Mexico City</a></div>
<p>Street parking in urban neighborhoods is mostly controlled by the <i><a href="/wiki/Franelero" title="Franelero">franeleros</a></i> a.k.a. "<i>viene vienes</i>" (lit. "come on, come on"), who ask drivers for a fee to park. Double parking is common (with <i>franeleros</i> moving the cars as required), impeding on the available lanes for traffic to pass. In order to mitigate that and other problems and to raise revenue,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[193]</a></sup> 721 parking meters (as of October 2013), have been installed in the west-central neighborhoods <a href="/wiki/Lomas_de_Chapultepec" title="Lomas de Chapultepec">Lomas de Chapultepec</a>, <a href="/wiki/Condesa" title="Condesa">Condesa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colonia_Roma" title="Colonia Roma">Roma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Polanco,_Mexico_City" title="Polanco, Mexico City">Polanco</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Anzures&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Anzures (page does not exist)">Anzures</a>, in operation from 8 AM to 8 PM on weekdays and charging a rate of 2 pesos per 15 minutes, with offenders' cars booted, costing about 500 pesos to remove. 30 percent of the monthly 16 million-peso (as of October 2013) income from the parking-meter system (named "ecoParq") is earmarked for neighborhood improvements. The granting of the license for all zones exclusively to a new company without experience in operating parking meters, Operadora de Estacionamientos Bicentenario, has generated controversy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[194]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cycling">Cycling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Cycling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Ecobici_(Mexico_City)" title="Ecobici (Mexico City)">Ecobici (Mexico City)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9031.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2848" data-file-width="4288" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9031.jpg/220px-15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9031.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9031.jpg/330px-15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9031.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9031.jpg/440px-15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9031.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:15-07-12-Mexico-D-F-RalfR-N3S_9031.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bicycles available for rental in <a href="/wiki/Zona_Rosa,_Mexico_City" title="Zona Rosa, Mexico City">Zona Rosa</a></div></div></div>
<p>The local government continuously strives for a reduction of massive traffic congestion, and has increased incentives for making a <a href="/wiki/Bicycle-friendly" title="Bicycle-friendly">bicycle-friendly</a> city. This includes North America's second-largest <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicycle_sharing_system" title="Bicycle sharing system">bicycle sharing system</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ecobici_(Mexico_City)" title="Ecobici (Mexico City)">Ecobici</a>, launched in 2010, in which registered residents can get bicycles for 45 minutes with a pre-paid subscription of 300 pesos a year. There are, as of September 2013, 276 stations with 4,000 bicycles across an area stretching from the <a href="/wiki/Historic_center_of_Mexico_City" title="Historic center of Mexico City">Historic center</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polanco_(Mexico)" title="Polanco (Mexico)">Polanco</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[195]</a></sup> within 300 meters (980 feet) of one another and are fully automatic using a transponder based card. Bicycle-service users have access to several permanent <a href="/wiki/Ciclov%C3%ADa" title="Ciclovía">Ciclovías</a> (dedicated bike paths/lanes/streets), including ones along <a href="/wiki/Paseo_de_la_Reforma" title="Paseo de la Reforma">Paseo de la Reforma</a> and Avenida Chapultepec as well as one running 59 kilometers (37 miles) from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Polanco_(Mexico)" title="Polanco (Mexico)">Polanco</a> to <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Fierro_del_Toro&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Fierro del Toro (page does not exist)">Fierro del Toro</a>, which is located south of <a href="/wiki/Cumbres_del_Ajusco_National_Park" title="Cumbres del Ajusco National Park">Cumbres del Ajusco National Park</a>, near the <a href="/wiki/Morelos" title="Morelos">Morelos</a> state line.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-197"><a href="#cite_note-197">[196]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-198"><a href="#cite_note-198">[197]</a></sup> The city's initiative is inspired by forward thinking examples, such as <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">Denmark</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Copenhagenization_(bicycling)" title="Copenhagenization (bicycling)">Copenhagenization</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Art">Art</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Art">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Mexican_art" title="Mexican art">Mexican art</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Atardecer_En_Bellas_Artes_Horizontal_(128312025).jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1366" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Atardecer_En_Bellas_Artes_Horizontal_%28128312025%29.jpeg/220px-Atardecer_En_Bellas_Artes_Horizontal_%28128312025%29.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Atardecer_En_Bellas_Artes_Horizontal_%28128312025%29.jpeg/330px-Atardecer_En_Bellas_Artes_Horizontal_%28128312025%29.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Atardecer_En_Bellas_Artes_Horizontal_%28128312025%29.jpeg/440px-Atardecer_En_Bellas_Artes_Horizontal_%28128312025%29.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Atardecer_En_Bellas_Artes_Horizontal_(128312025).jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">Art Nouveau</a>/Neoclassical <a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_Bellas_Artes" title="Palacio de Bellas Artes">Palacio de Bellas Artes</a> is the prominent cultural center in the city</div></div></div>
<p>Having been capital of a vast pre-Hispanic empire, and also the capital of richest viceroyalty within the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> (ruling over a vast territory in the Americas and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_West_Indies" title="Spanish West Indies">Spanish West Indies</a>), and, finally, the capital of the United Mexican States, Mexico City has a rich history of <a href="/wiki/Mexican_art" title="Mexican art">artistic expression</a>. Since the mesoamerican pre-Classical period the inhabitants of the settlements around Lake Texcoco produced many works of art and complex craftsmanship, some of which are today displayed at the world-renowned <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Museo_Nacional_de_Antropolog%C3%ADa" title="Museo Nacional de Antropología">National Museum of Anthropology</a> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Templo_Mayor" title="Templo Mayor">Templo Mayor</a></i> museum. While many pieces of pottery and stone-engraving have survived, the great majority of the Amerindian iconography was destroyed during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conquest_of_the_Aztec_Empire" title="Conquest of the Aztec Empire">conquest of the Aztec Empire</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Much of the early colonial art stemmed from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aztec_codices" title="Aztec codices">Aztec codices</a>, aiming to recover and preserve some Aztec and other Amerindian iconography and history. From then, artistic expressions in Mexico were mostly religious in theme. The <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_Metropolitan_Cathedral" title="Mexico City Metropolitan Cathedral">Metropolitan Cathedral</a> still displays works by <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Juan_de_Rojas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Juan de Rojas (page does not exist)">Juan de Rojas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Juan_Correa" title="Juan Correa">Juan Correa</a> and an <a href="/wiki/Oil_painting" title="Oil painting">oil painting</a> whose authorship has been attributed to <a href="/wiki/Bartolom%C3%A9_Esteban_Murillo" title="Bartolomé Esteban Murillo">Murillo</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Secular works of art of this period include the <a href="/wiki/Equestrian_statue" title="Equestrian statue">equestrian sculpture</a> of <a href="/wiki/Charles_IV_of_Spain" title="Charles IV of Spain">Charles IV of Spain</a>, locally known as <i>El Caballito</i> ("The little horse"). This piece, in bronze, was the work of <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Tols%C3%A1" title="Manuel Tolsá">Manuel Tolsá</a> and it has been placed at the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Plaza_Tols%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Plaza Tolsá (page does not exist)">Plaza Tolsá</a>, in front of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palacio_de_Mineria" title="Palacio de Mineria">Palacio de Mineria</a> (Mining Palace). Directly in front of this building is the <a href="/wiki/Museo_Nacional_de_Arte" title="Museo Nacional de Arte">Museo Nacional de Arte</a> (Munal) (the National Museum of Art).
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ReceptHallMUNAL.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3872" data-file-width="2592" decoding="async" height="254" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/ReceptHallMUNAL.JPG/170px-ReceptHallMUNAL.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/ReceptHallMUNAL.JPG/255px-ReceptHallMUNAL.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/ReceptHallMUNAL.JPG/340px-ReceptHallMUNAL.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ReceptHallMUNAL.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Receptions Hall at the <a href="/wiki/Museo_Nacional_de_Arte" title="Museo Nacional de Arte">Museo Nacional de Arte</a></div></div></div>
<p>During the 19th century, an important producer of art was the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_San_Carlos" title="Academy of San Carlos">Academia de San Carlos</a> (San Carlos Art Academy), founded during colonial times, and which later became the Escuela Nacional de Artes Plásticas (the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_School_of_Arts_(UNAM)" title="National School of Arts (UNAM)">National School of Arts</a>) including painting, sculpture and graphic design, one of UNAM's <a href="/wiki/Art_school" title="Art school">art schools</a>. Many of the works produced by the students and faculty of that time are now displayed in the Museo Nacional de San Carlos (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_San_Carlos" title="National Museum of San Carlos">National Museum of San Carlos</a>). One of the students, <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Velasco_G%C3%B3mez" title="José María Velasco Gómez">José María Velasco</a>, is considered one of the greatest Mexican landscape painters of the 19th century. <a href="/wiki/Porfirio_D%C3%ADaz" title="Porfirio Díaz">Porfirio Díaz</a>'s regime sponsored arts, especially those that followed the French school. Popular arts in the form of cartoons and illustrations flourished, e.g. those of <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Guadalupe_Posada" title="José Guadalupe Posada">José Guadalupe Posada</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Manuel_Manilla&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Manuel Manilla (page does not exist)">Manuel Manilla</a>. The permanent collection of the San Carlos Museum also includes paintings by European masters such as Rembrandt, Velázquez, Murillo, and Rubens.
</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Revolution" title="Mexican Revolution">Mexican Revolution</a>, an <a href="/wiki/Avant-garde" title="Avant-garde">avant-garde</a> <a href="/wiki/Art_movement" title="Art movement">artistic movement</a> originated in Mexico City: <a href="/wiki/Mural" title="Mural">muralism</a>. Many of the works of muralists <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Clemente_Orozco" title="José Clemente Orozco">José Clemente Orozco</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Alfaro_Siqueiros" title="David Alfaro Siqueiros">David Alfaro Siqueiros</a> and <a href="/wiki/Diego_Rivera" title="Diego Rivera">Diego Rivera</a> are displayed in numerous buildings in the city, most notably at the <a href="/wiki/National_Palace_(Mexico)" title="National Palace (Mexico)">National Palace</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_Bellas_Artes" title="Palacio de Bellas Artes">Palacio de Bellas Artes</a>. <a href="/wiki/Frida_Kahlo" title="Frida Kahlo">Frida Kahlo</a>, wife of Rivera, with a strong nationalist expression, was also one of the most renowned of Mexican painters. Her house has become a museum that displays many of her works.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-199"><a href="#cite_note-199">[198]</a></sup>
</p><p>The former home of Rivera muse <a href="/wiki/Dolores_Olmedo" title="Dolores Olmedo">Dolores Olmedo</a> houses the namesake museum. The facility is in Xochimilco borough in southern Mexico City and includes several buildings surrounded by sprawling manicured lawns. It houses a large collection of Rivera and Kahlo paintings and drawings, as well as living <i>Xoloizcuintles</i> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_Hairless_Dog" title="Mexican Hairless Dog">Mexican Hairless Dog</a>). It also regularly hosts small but important temporary exhibits of classical and <a href="/wiki/Modern_art" title="Modern art">modern art</a> (e.g. Venetian Masters and Contemporary New York artists).
</p><p>During the 20th century, many artists immigrated to Mexico City from different regions of Mexico, such as <a href="/wiki/Leopoldo_M%C3%A9ndez" title="Leopoldo Méndez">Leopoldo Méndez</a>, an engraver from Veracruz, who supported the creation of the socialist Taller de la Gráfica Popular (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Popular_Graphics_Workshop&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Popular Graphics Workshop (page does not exist)">Popular Graphics Workshop</a>), designed to help <a href="/wiki/Blue-collar_worker" title="Blue-collar worker">blue-collar</a> workers find a venue to express their art. Other painters came from abroad, such as <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalan</a> painter <a href="/wiki/Remedios_Varo" title="Remedios Varo">Remedios Varo</a> and other Spanish and Jewish exiles. It was in the second half of the 20th century that the artistic movement began to drift apart from the Revolutionary theme. <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Luis_Cuevas" title="José Luis Cuevas">José Luis Cuevas</a> opted for a modernist style in contrast to the muralist movement associated with social politics.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hochob_Campeche_-_Rekonstruktion_des_Tempels.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Hochob_Campeche_-_Rekonstruktion_des_Tempels.jpg/220px-Hochob_Campeche_-_Rekonstruktion_des_Tempels.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Hochob_Campeche_-_Rekonstruktion_des_Tempels.jpg/330px-Hochob_Campeche_-_Rekonstruktion_des_Tempels.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Hochob_Campeche_-_Rekonstruktion_des_Tempels.jpg/440px-Hochob_Campeche_-_Rekonstruktion_des_Tempels.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hochob_Campeche_-_Rekonstruktion_des_Tempels.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Reconstruction of the entrance to the Hochob temple in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Anthropology" title="National Museum of Anthropology">National Museum of Anthropology</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Museo_Soumaya_Plaza.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3632" data-file-width="4848" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Museo_Soumaya_Plaza.jpg/220px-Museo_Soumaya_Plaza.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Museo_Soumaya_Plaza.jpg/330px-Museo_Soumaya_Plaza.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Museo_Soumaya_Plaza.jpg/440px-Museo_Soumaya_Plaza.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Museo_Soumaya_Plaza.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Museo_Soumaya" title="Museo Soumaya">Museo Soumaya</a></div></div></div>
<p>Mexico City has numerous museums dedicated to art, including Mexican colonial, modern and <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_art" title="Contemporary art">contemporary art</a>, and international art. The Museo Tamayo was opened in the mid-1980s to house the collection of international contemporary art donated by Mexican painter <a href="/wiki/Rufino_Tamayo" title="Rufino Tamayo">Rufino Tamayo</a>. The collection includes pieces by Picasso, Klee, Kandinsky, Warhol and many others, though most of the collection is stored while visiting exhibits are shown. The <a href="/wiki/Museo_de_Arte_Moderno" title="Museo de Arte Moderno">Museo de Arte Moderno</a> is a repository of Mexican artists from the 20th century, including Rivera, Orozco, Siqueiros, Kahlo, <a href="/wiki/Gunther_Gerzso" title="Gunther Gerzso">Gerzso</a>, Carrington, Tamayo, and also regularly hosts temporary exhibits of international modern art. In southern Mexico City, the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Carrillo_Gil_Museum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Carrillo Gil Museum (page does not exist)">Carrillo Gil Museum</a> showcases avant-garde artists, as does the <a href="/wiki/Museo_Universitario_Arte_Contempor%C3%A1neo" title="Museo Universitario Arte Contemporáneo">Museo Universitario Arte Contemporáneo</a>, designed by Mexican architect <a href="/wiki/Teodoro_Gonz%C3%A1lez_de_Le%C3%B3n" title="Teodoro González de León">Teodoro González de León</a>, inaugurated in late 2008.
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Museo_Soumaya" title="Museo Soumaya">Museo Soumaya</a>, named after the wife of Mexican magnate <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Slim" title="Carlos Slim">Carlos Slim</a>, has the largest private collection of original <a href="/wiki/Auguste_Rodin" title="Auguste Rodin">Rodin</a> sculptures outside of France.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-200"><a href="#cite_note-200">[199]</a></sup> It also has a large collection of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dal%C3%AD" title="Dalí">Dalí</a> sculptures, and recently began showing pieces in its masters collection including <a href="/wiki/El_Greco" title="El Greco">El Greco</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vel%C3%A1zquez" title="Velázquez">Velázquez</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Picasso" title="Picasso">Picasso</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canaletto" title="Canaletto">Canaletto</a>. The museum inaugurated a new futuristic-design facility in 2011 just north of Polanco, while maintaining a smaller facility in <a href="/wiki/Museo_Soumaya#Plaza_Loreto" title="Museo Soumaya">Plaza Loreto</a> in southern Mexico City. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colecci%C3%B3n_J%C3%BAmex" title="Colección Júmex">Colección Júmex</a> is a contemporary art museum located on the sprawling grounds of the <a href="/wiki/Jumex" title="Jumex">Jumex</a> juice company in the northern industrial suburb of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Crist%C3%B3bal_Ecatepec" title="San Cristóbal Ecatepec">Ecatepec</a>. It has the largest private contemporary art collection in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> and hosts pieces from its permanent collection as well as traveling exhibits. The Museo de San Ildefonso, housed in the Antiguo Colegio de San Ildefonso in Mexico City's historic downtown district is a 17th-century colonnaded palace housing an art museum that regularly hosts world-class exhibits of Mexican and international art. The <a href="/wiki/Museo_Nacional_de_Arte" title="Museo Nacional de Arte">Museo Nacional de Arte</a> is also located in a former palace in the historic center. It houses a large collection of pieces by all major Mexican artists of the last 400 years and also hosts visiting exhibits.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jack_Kerouac" title="Jack Kerouac">Jack Kerouac</a>, the noted American author, spent extended periods of time in the city, and wrote his 1959 masterpiece volume of poetry <i><a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_Blues" title="Mexico City Blues">Mexico City Blues</a></i> here. Another American author, <a href="/wiki/William_S._Burroughs" title="William S. Burroughs">William S. Burroughs</a>, also lived in <a href="/wiki/Colonia_Roma" title="Colonia Roma">Colonia Roma</a> where he accidentally shot his wife. Most of Mexico City's museums can be visited from Tuesday to Sunday from 10am to 5pm, although some of them have extended schedules, such as the Museum of Anthropology and History, which is open to 7pm. In addition to this, entrance to most museums are free on Sunday. In some cases a modest fee may be charged.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-201"><a href="#cite_note-201">[200]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Memory_and_Tolerance_Museum" title="Memory and Tolerance Museum">Memory and Tolerance Museum</a>, inaugurated in 2011, showcases historical events of discrimination and genocide. Permanent exhibits include those on the Holocaust and other large-scale atrocities. It also houses temporary exhibits; one on <a href="/wiki/Tibet" title="Tibet">Tibet</a> was inaugurated by the <a href="/wiki/Dalai_Lama" title="Dalai Lama">Dalai Lama</a> in September 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-202"><a href="#cite_note-202">[201]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Music.2C_theater_and_entertainment"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Music,_theater_and_entertainment">Music, theater and entertainment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Music, theater and entertainment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Teatro_de_la_Ciudad_de_Mexico.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1024" data-file-width="768" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Teatro_de_la_Ciudad_de_Mexico.jpg/170px-Teatro_de_la_Ciudad_de_Mexico.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Teatro_de_la_Ciudad_de_Mexico.jpg/255px-Teatro_de_la_Ciudad_de_Mexico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/Teatro_de_la_Ciudad_de_Mexico.jpg/340px-Teatro_de_la_Ciudad_de_Mexico.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Teatro_de_la_Ciudad_de_Mexico.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Teatro_de_la_Ciudad" title="Teatro de la Ciudad">City Theatre</a> built in 1918.</div></div></div>
<p>Mexico City is home to a number of orchestras offering season programs. These include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexico_City_Philharmonic" title="Mexico City Philharmonic">Mexico City Philharmonic</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-203"><a href="#cite_note-203">[202]</a></sup> which performs at the Sala Ollin Yoliztli; the <a href="/wiki/National_Symphony_Orchestra_(Mexico)" title="National Symphony Orchestra (Mexico)">National Symphony Orchestra</a>, whose home base is the <a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_Bellas_Artes" title="Palacio de Bellas Artes">Palacio de Bellas Artes</a> (Palace of the <a href="/wiki/Fine_art" title="Fine art">Fine Arts</a>), a masterpiece of <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">art nouveau</a> and art decó styles; the <a href="/wiki/Orchestra" title="Orchestra">Philharmonic Orchestra</a> of the National Autonomous University of Mexico (<a href="/wiki/OFUNAM" title="OFUNAM">OFUNAM</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-204"><a href="#cite_note-204">[203]</a></sup> and the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Miner%C3%ADa_Symphony_Orchestra&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Minería Symphony Orchestra (page does not exist)">Minería Symphony Orchestra</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[204]</a></sup> both of which perform at the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Sala_Nezahualc%C3%B3yotl&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Sala Nezahualcóyotl (page does not exist)">Sala Nezahualcóyotl</a>, which was the first wrap-around concert hall of the world's western hemisphere when inaugurated in 1976. There are also many smaller ensembles that enrich the city's musical scene, including the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Carlos_Ch%C3%A1vez_Youth_Symphony&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Carlos Chávez Youth Symphony (page does not exist)">Carlos Chávez Youth Symphony</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Cuarteto_Latinoamericano" title="Cuarteto Latinoamericano">Cuarteto Latinoamericano</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_World_Symphony_Orchestra" title="New World Symphony Orchestra">New World Orchestra</a> (Orquesta del Nuevo Mundo), the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=National_Polytechnical_Symphony&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="National Polytechnical Symphony (page does not exist)">National Polytechnical Symphony</a> and the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bellas_Artes_Chamber_Orchestra&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bellas Artes Chamber Orchestra (page does not exist)">Bellas Artes Chamber Orchestra</a> (Orquesta de Cámara de Bellas Artes).
</p><p>The city is also a leading center of <a href="/wiki/Popular_culture" title="Popular culture">popular culture</a> and music. There are a multitude of venues hosting Spanish and foreign-language performers. These include the 10,000-seat <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Auditorium" title="National Auditorium">National Auditorium</a> that regularly schedules the Spanish and English-language pop and rock artists, as well as many of the world's leading <a href="/wiki/Performing_arts" title="Performing arts">performing arts</a> ensembles, the auditorium also broadcasts <a href="/wiki/Grand_opera" title="Grand opera">grand opera</a> performances from New York's <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_Opera" title="Metropolitan Opera">Metropolitan Opera</a> on giant, high definition screens. In 2007 National Auditorium was selected world's best venue by multiple genre media. Other sites for pop-artist performances include the 3,000-seat <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Teatro_Metropolitan" title="Teatro Metropolitan">Teatro Metropolitan</a>, the 15,000-seat <a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_los_Deportes" title="Palacio de los Deportes">Palacio de los Deportes</a>, and the larger 50,000-seat <a href="/wiki/Foro_Sol" title="Foro Sol">Foro Sol</a> Stadium, where popular international artists perform on a regular basis. The <a href="/wiki/Cirque_du_Soleil" title="Cirque du Soleil">Cirque du Soleil</a> has held several seasons at the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Carpa_Santa_Fe&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Carpa Santa Fe (page does not exist)">Carpa Santa Fe</a>, in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Fe_(Mexico_City)" title="Santa Fe (Mexico City)">Santa Fe</a> district in the western part of the city. There are numerous venues for smaller musical ensembles and solo performers. These include the <a href="/wiki/Hard_Rock_Live" title="Hard Rock Live">Hard Rock Live</a>, Bataclán, Foro Scotiabank, Lunario, Circo Volador and Voilá Acoustique. Recent additions include the 20,000-seat <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arena_Ciudad_de_M%C3%A9xico" title="Arena Ciudad de México">Arena Ciudad de México</a>, the 3,000-seat Pepsi Center World Trade Center, and the 2,500-seat Auditorio Blackberry.
</p><p>The Centro Nacional de las Artes (<a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=National_Center_for_the_Arts&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="National Center for the Arts (page does not exist)">National Center for the Arts</a>) has several venues for music, theater, dance. UNAM's main campus, also in the southern part of the city, is home to the Centro Cultural Universitario (the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=University_Culture_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="University Culture Center (page does not exist)">University Culture Center</a>) (CCU). The CCU also houses the <a href="/wiki/National_Library_of_Mexico" title="National Library of Mexico">National Library</a>, the interactive <a href="/wiki/Universum_(UNAM)" title="Universum (UNAM)">Universum, Museo de las Ciencias</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-206"><a href="#cite_note-206">[205]</a></sup> the Sala Nezahualcóyotl concert hall, several theaters and cinemas, and the new <a href="/wiki/Museo_Universitario_Arte_Contempor%C3%A1neo" title="Museo Universitario Arte Contemporáneo">University Museum of Contemporary Art</a> (MUAC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-207"><a href="#cite_note-207">[206]</a></sup> A branch of the National University's CCU cultural center was inaugurated in 2007 in the facilities of the former <a href="/wiki/Foreign_minister" title="Foreign minister">Ministry of Foreign Affairs</a>, known as Tlatelolco, in north-central Mexico City.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Fachada_de_la_Biblioteca_Vasconcelos_Buenavista_Ciudad_de_M%C3%A9xico.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4928" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Fachada_de_la_Biblioteca_Vasconcelos_Buenavista_Ciudad_de_M%C3%A9xico.jpg/220px-Fachada_de_la_Biblioteca_Vasconcelos_Buenavista_Ciudad_de_M%C3%A9xico.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Fachada_de_la_Biblioteca_Vasconcelos_Buenavista_Ciudad_de_M%C3%A9xico.jpg/330px-Fachada_de_la_Biblioteca_Vasconcelos_Buenavista_Ciudad_de_M%C3%A9xico.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Fachada_de_la_Biblioteca_Vasconcelos_Buenavista_Ciudad_de_M%C3%A9xico.jpg/440px-Fachada_de_la_Biblioteca_Vasconcelos_Buenavista_Ciudad_de_M%C3%A9xico.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Fachada_de_la_Biblioteca_Vasconcelos_Buenavista_Ciudad_de_M%C3%A9xico.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Biblioteca_Vasconcelos" title="Biblioteca Vasconcelos">Biblioteca Vasconcelos</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Vasconcelos_Library" title="José Vasconcelos Library">José Vasconcelos Library</a>, a national library, is located on the grounds of the former Buenavista railroad station in the northern part of the city. The <a href="/wiki/Papalote_Museo_del_Ni%C3%B1o" title="Papalote Museo del Niño">Papalote Museo del Niño</a> (Kite Children's Museum), which houses the world's largest dome screen, is located in the wooded park of <a href="/wiki/Chapultepec" title="Chapultepec">Chapultepec</a>, near the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Museo_Tecnol%C3%B3gico&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Museo Tecnológico (page does not exist)">Museo Tecnológico</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_Feria_de_Chapultepec_M%C3%A1gico" title="La Feria de Chapultepec Mágico">La Feria</a>, a former <a href="/wiki/Amusement_park" title="Amusement park">amusement park</a>. The theme park <a href="/wiki/Six_Flags_M%C3%A9xico" title="Six Flags México">Six Flags México</a> (the largest amusement park in Latin America) is located in the <a href="/wiki/Ajusco" title="Ajusco">Ajusco</a> neighborhood, in Tlalpan borough, southern Mexico City. During the winter, the main square of the <a href="/wiki/Z%C3%B3calo" title="Zócalo">Zócalo</a> is transformed into a gigantic <a href="/wiki/Ice_rink" title="Ice rink">ice skating rink</a>, which is said to be the largest in the world behind that of Moscow's <a href="/wiki/Red_Square" title="Red Square">Red Square</a>.
</p><p>The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Cineteca_Nacional&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cineteca Nacional (page does not exist)">Cineteca Nacional</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;"> [<a class="extiw" href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cineteca_Nacional" title="es:Cineteca Nacional">es</a>]</span> (Mexican Film Library), near the Coyoacán suburb, shows a variety of films, and stages many film festivals, including the annual <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Muestra_Internacional_de_Cine&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Muestra Internacional de Cine (page does not exist)">International Showcase</a>, and many smaller ones ranging from Scandinavian and Uruguayan cinema, to Jewish and LGBT-themed films. <a href="/wiki/Cin%C3%A9polis" title="Cinépolis">Cinépolis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cinemex" title="Cinemex">Cinemex</a>, the two biggest film <a href="/wiki/Chain_store" title="Chain store">business chains</a>, also have several film festivals throughout the year, with both national and international movies. Mexico City has a number of <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> theaters, providing residents and visitors access to films ranging from documentaries to blockbusters on these large screens.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Mexico_City" title="Cuisine of Mexico City">Cuisine of Mexico City</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Street_tacos_in_Mexico_City_(8495923877).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1767" data-file-width="2087" decoding="async" height="186" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Street_tacos_in_Mexico_City_%288495923877%29.jpg/220px-Street_tacos_in_Mexico_City_%288495923877%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Street_tacos_in_Mexico_City_%288495923877%29.jpg/330px-Street_tacos_in_Mexico_City_%288495923877%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Street_tacos_in_Mexico_City_%288495923877%29.jpg/440px-Street_tacos_in_Mexico_City_%288495923877%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Street_tacos_in_Mexico_City_(8495923877).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Street_food" title="Street food">Street</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tacos" title="Tacos">tacos</a> in Mexico City</div></div></div>
<p>Once considered plebeian fare, by the 19th century tacos had become a standard of Mexico City's cuisine. Furthermore, as authorities struggled to tax local <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taquerias" title="Taquerias">taquerias</a>, imposing licensing requirements and penalties, they recorded some details of the types of foods being served by these establishments. The most frequent reference was for <i>tacos de <a href="/wiki/Barbacoa" title="Barbacoa">barbacoa</a></i>. Also mentioned are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enchiladas" title="Enchiladas">enchiladas</a>, <i>tacos de minero</i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gorditas" title="Gorditas">gorditas</a></i>, along with oyster shops and fried fish stands. There is evidence of some regional specialties being made available for recent migrants; at least two shops were known to serve <i><a href="/wiki/Pozole" title="Pozole">pozole</a></i>, a type of stew similar to <a href="/wiki/Hominy" title="Hominy">hominy</a> that is a staple of <a href="/wiki/Guadalajara" title="Guadalajara">Guadalajara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jalisco" title="Jalisco">Jalisco</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-208"><a href="#cite_note-208">[207]</a></sup> Mexico City is known for having some of the freshest fish and seafood in Mexico's interior. <a href="/wiki/La_Nueva_Viga_Market" title="La Nueva Viga Market">La Nueva Viga Market</a> is the second largest seafood market in the world after the <a href="/wiki/Tsukiji_fish_market" title="Tsukiji fish market">Tsukiji fish market</a> in Japan.
</p><p>Mexico City offers a variety of cuisines: restaurants specializing in the regional cuisines of Mexico's 31 states are available in the city, and the city also has several branches of internationally recognized restaurants. These include Paris' Au Pied de Cochon and <a href="/wiki/Brasserie_Lipp" title="Brasserie Lipp">Brasserie Lipp</a>, Philippe (by Philippe Chow); Nobu, Quintonil, Morimoto; Pámpano, owned by Mexican-raised opera singer <a href="/wiki/Pl%C3%A1cido_Domingo" title="Plácido Domingo">Plácido Domingo</a>. There are branches of <a href="/wiki/Japanese_cuisine" title="Japanese cuisine">Japanese</a> restaurant <a href="/wiki/Suntory" title="Suntory">Suntory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_cuisine" title="Italian cuisine">Italian</a> restaurant Alfredo, as well as New York steakhouses <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Morton%27s_Restaurant_Group" title="Morton's Restaurant Group">Morton's</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Palm_(restaurant)" title="The Palm (restaurant)">The Palm</a>, and Monte Carlo's BeefBar. Three of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lima,_Peru" title="Lima, Peru">Lima</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Haute_cuisine" title="Haute cuisine">Haute</a> restaurants, serving <a href="/wiki/Peruvian_cuisine" title="Peruvian cuisine">Peruvian cuisine</a>, have locations in Mexico City: La Mar, Segundo Muelle and Astrid y Gastón.
</p><p>For the 2019 list of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Restaurant_(magazine)_Top_50" title="Restaurant (magazine) Top 50">World's 50 Best Restaurants</a> as named by the British magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Restaurant_(magazine)" title="Restaurant (magazine)">Restaurant</a></i>, Mexico City ranked 12th best with the Mexican avant-garde restaurant <a href="/wiki/Pujol_(restaurant)" title="Pujol (restaurant)">Pujol</a> (owned by Mexican chef Enrique Olvera). Also notable is the Basque-Mexican fusion restaurant <a href="/wiki/Biko_(restaurant)" title="Biko (restaurant)">Biko</a> (run and co-owned by Bruno Oteiza and Mikel Alonso), which placed outside the list at 59th, but in previous years has ranked within the top 50.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2014_awards_209-0"><a href="#cite_note-2014_awards-209">[208]</a></sup> Other that has been placed on the list in 2019 is the restaurant Sud 777 at 58th place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[209]</a></sup> At the other end of the scale are working class <a href="/wiki/Pulque" title="Pulque">pulque</a> bars known as <i>pulquerías</i>, a challenge for tourists to locate and experience.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TELEVISA_CHAPULTEPEC.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="854" data-file-width="1205" decoding="async" height="156" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/TELEVISA_CHAPULTEPEC.jpg/220px-TELEVISA_CHAPULTEPEC.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/TELEVISA_CHAPULTEPEC.jpg/330px-TELEVISA_CHAPULTEPEC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/TELEVISA_CHAPULTEPEC.jpg/440px-TELEVISA_CHAPULTEPEC.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TELEVISA_CHAPULTEPEC.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Televisa" title="Televisa">Televisa</a> headquarters in Mexico City</div></div></div>
<p>Mexico City is the Mexico's most important for the printed media and <a href="/wiki/Publishing" title="Publishing">book publishing</a> industries. Dozens of daily newspapers are published, including <i><a href="/wiki/El_Universal_(Mexico_City)" title="El Universal (Mexico City)">El Universal</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Exc%C3%A9lsior" title="Excélsior">Excélsior</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Reforma" title="Reforma">Reforma</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/La_Jornada" title="La Jornada">La Jornada</a></i>. Other major papers include <i><a href="/wiki/Milenio" title="Milenio">Milenio</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cr%C3%B3nica,_Buenos_Aires" title="Crónica, Buenos Aires">Crónica</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/El_Economista_(Mexico)" title="El Economista (Mexico)">El Economista</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/El_Financiero" title="El Financiero">El Financiero</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SIC_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-SIC-211">[210]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[211]</a></sup> Leading magazines include <i><a href="/wiki/Expansi%C3%B3n_(Mexico)" title="Expansión (Mexico)">Expansión</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Proceso_(magazine)" title="Proceso (magazine)">Proceso</a></i>, <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Poder&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Poder (page does not exist)">Poder</a></i>, as well as dozens of entertainment publications such as <i><a href="/wiki/Vanidades" title="Vanidades">Vanidades</a></i>, <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Qui%C3%A9n_(magazine)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Quién (magazine) (page does not exist)">Quién</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Chilango" title="Chilango">Chilango</a></i>, <i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=TVNotas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="TVNotas (page does not exist)">TV Notas</a></i>, and local editions of <i><a href="/wiki/Vogue_(magazine)" title="Vogue (magazine)">Vogue</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/GQ" title="GQ">GQ</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Architectural_Digest" title="Architectural Digest">Architectural Digest</a></i>.
</p><p>It is also a leading center of the <a href="/wiki/Advertising_industry" title="Advertising industry">advertizing industry</a>. Most international ad firms have offices in the city, including Grey, <a href="/wiki/J._Walter_Thompson" title="J. Walter Thompson">JWT</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leo_Burnett" title="Leo Burnett">Leo Burnett</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euro_RSCG" title="Euro RSCG">Euro RSCG</a>, <a href="/wiki/BBDO" title="BBDO">BBDO</a>, Ogilvy, <a href="/wiki/Saatchi_%26_Saatchi" title="Saatchi &amp; Saatchi">Saatchi &amp; Saatchi</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McCann_Erickson" title="McCann Erickson">McCann Erickson</a>. Many local firms also compete in the sector, including <a href="/wiki/Alazraki" title="Alazraki">Alazraki</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Olabuenaga/Chemistri&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Olabuenaga/Chemistri (page does not exist)">Olabuenaga/Chemistri</a>, Terán, Augusto Elías, and Clemente Cámara, among others. There are 60 <a href="/wiki/List_of_radio_stations_in_Mexico_City" title="List of radio stations in Mexico City">radio stations</a> operating in the city and many <a href="/wiki/Local_community" title="Local community">local community</a> radio transmission networks.
</p><p>The two largest media companies in the Spanish-speaking world, <a href="/wiki/Televisa" title="Televisa">Televisa</a> and <a href="/wiki/TV_Azteca" title="TV Azteca">TV Azteca</a>, are headquartered in Mexico City. Other <a href="/wiki/Television_channel" title="Television channel">local television</a> channels include:
</p><p><a href="/wiki/XHDF-TDT" title="XHDF-TDT">XHDF</a> 1 (Azteca Uno),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[212]</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/XEW-TDT" title="XEW-TDT">XEW</a> 2 (Televisa W),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[213]</a></sup>
<a href="/wiki/XHCTMX-TDT" title="XHCTMX-TDT">XHCTMX</a> 3,
<a href="/wiki/XHTV-TDT" title="XHTV-TDT">XHTV</a> 4,
<a href="/wiki/XHGC-TDT" title="XHGC-TDT">XHGC</a> 5,
<a href="/wiki/XHTDMX-TDT" title="XHTDMX-TDT">XHTDMX</a> 6,
<a href="/wiki/XHIMT-TDT" title="XHIMT-TDT">XHIMT</a> 7,
<a href="/wiki/XEQ-TDT" title="XEQ-TDT">XEQ</a> 9,
<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/XEIPN-TDT" title="XEIPN-TDT">XEIPN</a> 11,
<a href="/wiki/XHUNAM-TDT" title="XHUNAM-TDT">XHUNAM</a> 20,
<a href="/wiki/XHCDM-TDT" title="XHCDM-TDT">XHCDM</a> 21,
<a href="/wiki/XEIMT-TDT" title="XEIMT-TDT">XEIMT</a> 22,
<a href="/wiki/XHTRES-TDT" title="XHTRES-TDT">XHTRES</a> 28,
<a href="/wiki/XHTVM-TDT" title="XHTVM-TDT">XHTVM</a> 40 and
<a href="/wiki/XHHCU-TDT" title="XHHCU-TDT">XHHCU</a> 45.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ACMX16.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3000" data-file-width="4000" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/ACMX16.JPG/220px-ACMX16.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/ACMX16.JPG/330px-ACMX16.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/ACMX16.JPG/440px-ACMX16.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ACMX16.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_Arena" title="Mexico City Arena">Mexico City Arena</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Association football</a> is the country's most popular and most <a href="/wiki/Broadcasting_of_sports_events" title="Broadcasting of sports events">televised franchised sport</a>. Its important venues in Mexico City include the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Azteca_Stadium" title="Azteca Stadium">Azteca Stadium</a>, home to the <a href="/wiki/Mexico_national_football_team" title="Mexico national football team">Mexico national football team</a> and giants <a href="/wiki/Club_Am%C3%A9rica" title="Club América">América</a>, which can seat 91,653 fans, making it the biggest stadium in Latin America. The <a href="/wiki/Estadio_Ol%C3%ADmpico_Universitario" title="Estadio Olímpico Universitario">Olympic Stadium</a> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/University_City_of_Mexico" title="University City of Mexico">Ciudad Universitaria</a> is home to the football club giants <a href="/wiki/Club_Universidad_Nacional" title="Club Universidad Nacional">Universidad Nacional</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Seating_capacity" title="Seating capacity">seating capacity</a> of over 52,000. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Estadio_Azul" title="Estadio Azul">Estadio Azul</a>, which seats 33,042 fans, is near the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Center_Mexico_City" title="World Trade Center Mexico City">World Trade Center Mexico City</a> in the Nochebuena <a href="/wiki/Colonia_(Mexico)" title="Colonia (Mexico)">neighborhood</a>, and is home to the giants <a href="/wiki/Cruz_Azul" title="Cruz Azul">Cruz Azul</a>. The three teams are based in Mexico City and play in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primera_Divisi%C3%B3n_de_M%C3%A9xico" title="Primera División de México">First Division</a>; they are also part, with Guadalajara-based giants <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Club_Deportivo_Guadalajara" title="Club Deportivo Guadalajara">Club Deportivo Guadalajara</a>, of Mexico's traditional "Big Four". 
</p><p>The country hosted the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cup</a> in <a href="/wiki/1970_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1970 FIFA World Cup">1970</a> and <a href="/wiki/1986_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1986 FIFA World Cup">1986</a>, and Azteca Stadium is the first stadium in World Cup history to host the final twice.
