The city will be one of the host cities for the <a href="/wiki/2026_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2026 FIFA World Cup">2026 FIFA World Cup</a>. Mexico City is the first Latin American city to host the Olympic Games, having held the <a href="/wiki/1968_Summer_Olympics" title="1968 Summer Olympics">Summer Olympics</a> in 1968, winning bids against <a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lyon" title="Lyon">Lyon</a> and Detroit. The city hosted the 1955 and 1975 <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Games" title="Pan American Games">Pan American Games</a>, the last after Santiago and São Paulo withdrew. The <a href="/wiki/ICF_Canoe_Sprint_World_Championships" title="ICF Canoe Sprint World Championships">ICF Flatwater Racing World Championships</a> were hosted here in 1974 and 1994. <a href="/wiki/Lucha_libre" title="Lucha libre">Lucha libre</a> is a Mexican style of wrestling, and is one of the more popular sports throughout the country. The main venues in the city are <a href="/wiki/Arena_M%C3%A9xico" title="Arena México">Arena México</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arena_Coliseo" title="Arena Coliseo">Arena Coliseo</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aut%C3%B3dromo_Hermanos_Rodr%C3%ADguez,_June_4,_2018_SkySat_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1440" data-file-width="1920" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Aut%C3%B3dromo_Hermanos_Rodr%C3%ADguez%2C_June_4%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Aut%C3%B3dromo_Hermanos_Rodr%C3%ADguez%2C_June_4%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Aut%C3%B3dromo_Hermanos_Rodr%C3%ADguez%2C_June_4%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Aut%C3%B3dromo_Hermanos_Rodr%C3%ADguez%2C_June_4%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Aut%C3%B3dromo_Hermanos_Rodr%C3%ADguez%2C_June_4%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Aut%C3%B3dromo_Hermanos_Rodr%C3%ADguez%2C_June_4%2C_2018_SkySat_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aut%C3%B3dromo_Hermanos_Rodr%C3%ADguez,_June_4,_2018_SkySat_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Aut%C3%B3dromo_Hermanos_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Autódromo Hermanos Rodríguez">Autódromo Hermanos Rodríguez</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Aut%C3%B3dromo_Hermanos_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Autódromo Hermanos Rodríguez">Autódromo Hermanos Rodríguez</a> is the main venue for motorsport, and hosts the Formula 1 <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Grand_Prix" title="Mexican Grand Prix">Mexican Grand Prix</a> since its return to the sport in 2015, the event being held in the past from 1962 to 1970, and again from 1986 to 1992. From 1980 to 1981 and again from 2002 to 2007, the circuit hosted the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Champ_Car" title="Champ Car">Champ Car</a> World Series <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gran_Premio_de_M%C3%A9xico" title="Gran Premio de México">Gran Premio de México</a>. Beginning in 2005, the <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nationwide_Series" title="Nationwide Series">Nationwide Series</a> ran the <a href="/wiki/Corona_M%C3%A9xico_200" title="Corona México 200">Telcel-Motorola México 200</a>. 2005 also marked the first running of the Mexico City 250 by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_American_Road_Racing_Association" title="Grand American Road Racing Association">Grand-Am</a> <a href="/wiki/Rolex_Sports_Car_Series" title="Rolex Sports Car Series">Rolex Sports Car Series</a>. Both races were removed from their series' schedules for 2009.
</p><p>Baseball is another sport played professionally in the city. Mexico City is home of the <a href="/wiki/Diablos_Rojos_del_M%C3%A9xico" title="Diablos Rojos del México">Mexico City Red Devils</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_League_(baseball)" title="Mexican League (baseball)">Mexican League</a>, which is considered a Triple-A league by Major League Baseball. The Devils play their home games at <a href="/wiki/Estadio_Alfredo_Harp_Hel%C3%BA" title="Estadio Alfredo Harp Helú">Estadio Alfredo Harp Helú</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[214]</a></sup> designed by international Mexican-American architect <a class="external text" href="http://fgp-atelier.com" rel="nofollow">FGP Atelier</a> Founder <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Francisco_Gonzalez_Pulido" title="Francisco Gonzalez Pulido">Francisco Gonzalez Pulido</a> in collaboration with local architect Taller ADG.  Mexico City has some 10 Little Leagues for young baseball players. In 2005, Mexico City became the first city to host an <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">NFL</a> regular season game outside of the United States, at the <a href="/wiki/Estadio_Azteca" title="Estadio Azteca">Azteca Stadium</a>. The crowd of 103,467 people attending this game was the largest ever for a regular season game in NFL history until 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-216"><a href="#cite_note-216">[215]</a></sup>
</p><p>The city has also hosted several <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">NBA</a> pre-season games and has hosted international basketball's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FIBA_Americas_Championship" title="FIBA Americas Championship">FIBA Americas Championship</a>, along with north-of-the-border Major League Baseball exhibition games at <a href="/wiki/Foro_Sol" title="Foro Sol">Foro Sol</a>. In 2017, NBA commissioner <a href="/wiki/Adam_Silver" title="Adam Silver">Adam Silver</a> expressed interest in placing an <a href="/wiki/NBA_G_League" title="NBA G League">NBA G League</a> expansion team in Mexico City as early as 2018. This came to fruition on 12 December 2019 when commissioner Silver announced at a press conference in <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City_Arena" title="Mexico City Arena">Mexico City Arena</a> that <a href="/wiki/Liga_Nacional_de_Baloncesto_Profesional" title="Liga Nacional de Baloncesto Profesional">LNBP</a> team, <a href="/wiki/Capitanes_de_Ciudad_de_M%C3%A9xico" title="Capitanes de Ciudad de México">Capitanes de Ciudad de México</a> will be joining the G League in the 2020–21 season on a five-year agreement.
</p><p>Other sports facilities in Mexico City are the <a href="/wiki/Palacio_de_los_Deportes" title="Palacio de los Deportes">Palacio de los Deportes</a> indoor arena, <a href="/wiki/Alberca_Ol%C3%ADmpica_Francisco_M%C3%A1rquez" title="Alberca Olímpica Francisco Márquez">Francisco Márquez Olympic Swimming Pool</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Hip%C3%B3dromo_de_las_Am%C3%A9ricas" title="Hipódromo de las Américas">Hipódromo de Las Américas</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Agustin_Melgar_Olympic_Velodrome" title="Agustin Melgar Olympic Velodrome">Agustin Melgar Olympic Velodrome</a>, and venues for equestrianism and horse racing, ice hockey, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">rugby</a>, American-style football, baseball, and basketball. <a href="/wiki/Bullfighting" title="Bullfighting">Bullfighting</a> takes place every Sunday during bullfighting season at the 50,000-seat <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plaza_M%C3%A9xico" title="Plaza México">Plaza México</a>, the world's largest bullring. Mexico City's <a href="/wiki/Golf_course" title="Golf course">golf courses</a> have hosted Women's <a href="/wiki/LPGA" title="LPGA">LPGA</a> action, and two <a href="/wiki/World_Cup_(men%27s_golf)" title="World Cup (men's golf)">Men's Golf World Cups</a>. Courses throughout the city are available as private as well as public venues.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mexico_City&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_Spanish" title="Peninsular Spanish">Peninsular Spanish</a>, the spelling variant <i>Méjico</i>, is also used alongside <i>México</i>. According to the <i><a href="/wiki/Diccionario_panhisp%C3%A1nico_de_dudas" title="Diccionario panhispánico de dudas">Diccionario panhispánico de dudas</a></i> by the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Spanish_Academy" title="Royal Spanish Academy">Royal Spanish Academy</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Academies_of_the_Spanish_Language" title="Association of Academies of the Spanish Language">Association of Academies of the Spanish Language</a>, the spelling version with J is correct, however, the spelling with X is recommended, as it is the one is used in <a href="/wiki/Mexican_Spanish" title="Mexican Spanish">Mexican Spanish</a>.</span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>

<li id="cite_note-31"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-31">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1067248974" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><cite class="citation book cs1" id="CITEREFRamón_Gutiérrez_del_Mazo_(Intendent_of_Mexico:_1811–1821)1811">Ramón Gutiérrez del Mazo (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intendant_(government_official)" title="Intendant (government official)">Intendent</a> of Mexico: 1811–1821) (1811). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=IdygYgEACAAJ" rel="nofollow"><i>La muy noble, muy leal, insigne é imperial ciudad de México, cabeza de los reynos y provincias de Nueva España y en si nombre los señores presidente y vocales que componen la Real Junta de Policía de esta Córte con anuencia del Exmo. Sr. virey de este reyno hacemos saber al piadoso vecindario lo que sigue</i></a> [<i>The very noble, very loyal, distinguished and imperial city of Mexico, head of the kingdoms and provinces of New Spain and in its name the sirs president and members of the Royal Police Board of this Court with the consent of the Excellency Sr. Viceroy of this kingdom let the pious neighborhood know what's coming next</i>].</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=La+muy+noble%2C+muy+leal%2C+insigne+%C3%A9+imperial+ciudad+de+M%C3%A9xico%2C+cabeza+de+los+reynos+y+provincias+de+Nueva+Espa%C3%B1a+y+en+si+nombre+los+se%C3%B1ores+presidente+y+vocales+que+componen+la+Real+Junta+de+Polic%C3%ADa+de+esta+C%C3%B3rte+con+anuencia+del+Exmo.+Sr.+virey+de+este+reyno+hacemos+saber+al+piadoso+vecindario+lo+que+sigue&amp;rft.date=1811&amp;rft.au=Ram%C3%B3n+Guti%C3%A9rrez+del+Mazo+%28Intendent+of+Mexico%3A+1811%E2%80%931821%29&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DIdygYgEACAAJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AMexico+City"></span></span>

<li id="cite_note-WMO-103"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-WMO_103-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">
